However, floristic differences as well as the geographical and ecological relationships of the Carex davalliana-communities make it possible to distinguish five associations. Three associations are bound to the European mountains and are indicated by the simultaneous occurrence of Primula farinosa, Tofieldia calyculata, and Eleocharis quinqueflora: 1. Pediculari (silvaticae)-Caricetum davallianae is differentiated from the other two associations first of all by Primula integrifolia, Pedicularis mixta, and Selinum pyrenaeum. It occurs exclusively in the alpine zone of the Pyrenees. 2. Caricetum davallianae (s. str.) is characterized by several mountain to alpine species, e.g. Ballidiastrum michelii, Bartsia alpina, and Pinguicula alpina. It occurs in the territory of the Alps mostly at altitudes from 1000 to 2000 m.; it descends, however, also into the adjacent highlands as impoverished forms characterized only by Primula farinosa, Tofieldia calyculata, and Eleocharis quinqueflora. 3. Valeriano simplicifoliae-Caricetum davallianae is distributed over the Western Carpathians. From both the foregoing associations it is differentiated first of all by Valeriana simplicifolia and further by Galium vernum and Polygala amara ssp. brachyptera as differential species. The impoverished stands of this association are very similar to the impoverished stands of the alpine Caricetum davallianae. The further two associations occur in lower highlands and in lowlands of Central Europe. From the foregoing three associations they are differentiated by the absence of Primula farinosa, Tofieldia calyculata, and Eleocharis quinqueflora. There are the following associations: 4. Valeriano dioicae-Caricetum davallianae, characterized by higher occurrence constancy of Valeriana dioica and Caltha palustris; these species, however, cannot be considered as characteristic species. This association is distributed from the Eifel Mountains in Western Germany to the Hungarian Lowland at altitudes from 100 to 850 m. 5. Caricetum davalliano-demissae is differentiated from the foregoing association by a richer set of species of the order Caricetalia fuscae and the alliance Caricion fuscae, e.g. Carex stellulata, C. demissa, Juncus acutiflorus, J. bulbosus, Drosera rotundifolia, Sphagnum subsecundum, and S. recurvum; it represents therefore a member of the ecological series between the Valeriano dioicae-Caricetum davallianae and the acidophilous sedge-communities of the Caricion fuscae. At present this association is known only in the Schwarzwald Mountains. Within the associations those subassociations are mentioned which are of a more general validity. Moreover, those grounds have been discussed that were decisive in the syntaxonomical conception of particular associations and in the evaluation of the significance of particular species for the definition and delimitation of these associations. There follow several more general conclusions from this study concerning the classification of plant communities of particular units or group of related units in the whole area of distribution. 1. Units defined only on the basis of a few or only one characteristic species may be rather heterogeneous from both the floristic and the ecological point of view. Therefore it is advisable to consider the more important floristic differences of plant communities, of geographical origin, as differences of independent associations, especially if these units are geographically isolated. This evaluation is also supported by differences in the floristic composition of units caused by the fixation of the plant community in a pattern of plant communities which is characteristic for a particular territory. 2. The importance of a species for classification depends on the question of whether its occurrence in the community being studied lies in the range of its life prosperity or whether its prosperity is reduced and its occurrence in the community is conditioned only by penetration from surrounding communities. In evaluating the classificatory importance of a species (or several species) of lower constancy it ought be taken into consideration whether the probability of its occurrence is the same in all stands of the unit characterized by it, or whether in some stands this probability is lower or even nonexistent. Only where the occurrence probability of a species is equal for all stands included in the unit characterized by this species, even if it is not in all cases realized, is it possible to use the considered species for characterizing the unit. In this unit it is then possible to classify also stands where the characterizing species is absent but in which the occurrence probability of this species is the same as in the other stands of the unit. 3. The convergence phenomena can occur in stands of closely related units impoverished by species that differentiate the considered units. Such stands are nearly equal in their floristic composition but it is impossible to put them into the same unit because of differences in other characters than in the floristic composition. In such cases the occurrence probability of species characterizing the unit in the stands is to be judged. Only those impoverished stands may be put into one unit in which the occurrence probability of the species characterizing the unit the same is as in the normal stands. 4. The differentiation of closely related associations should be made from two standpoints: a) from the standpoint of the absolute relationships in the whole area of the group of related associations, b) from the standpoint of the relative relationships of association in a particular limited territory. The groups of species differentiating the related vicarious associations of different territories cannot be used in many cases for distinguishing these associations from closely related associations in one particular territory. In such cases a group of species which is usually common in all vicarious associations as well as specific for them must be used to differentiate associations. This group of species also expresses the specific environmental conditions of the considered group of vicarious associations. 
4180989|In the course of three years' investigations (1983-1986) of Lake Volvi, N Greece, 62 species and varieties of chlorococcal algae and 6 species of ulotrichal algae (Chlorophyceae) were found. Although chlorophytes form the largest group of the phytoplankton assemblages of the lake, their biomass is relatively small or even negligeable in some periods of the year in comparison with domination cyanophytes, diatoms and cryptophytes. Morphological variation of diagnostic features is described and documented by original drawings in 53 taxa.
4179780|A new species of the genus Tragopogon (T. kurdistanicum) has been described from Iraq.
4181272|A review is presented of various ecological and population aspects of Taraxacum agamospermy. Agamospermy is compared with vegetative clonality, the former differing in capability to generate variation, seed dispersal and often long evolutionary history. Clonal diversity of agamospermous taxa ranges from almost absolute uniclonality to high diversity of clones. Multiclonality is suggested to represent one of agamospecies' population characteristics. Biological individuality of clones allows coexistence of clones at a locality. Competition and other factors influencing number of clones at a locality are discussed. Geographical and ecological distributions of agamospermous and sexual Taraxacum taxa are evaluated, their coexistence and gene flow are addressed, and a hypothesis is presented concerning the population condition in mixed stands of sexual and asexual Taraxaca. Lastly, agamospermy is shown to significantly reduce recombination processes; it should not be considered an absolute evolutionary "blind alley".
4180690|The composition of volatile oils produced by Euphorbia fragifera is reported. The plant samples were collected in two different habitats on the Karst plateau North of Trieste (North Eastern Italy). The analysis was performed by capillary GC. Differences between samples from the two habitats have been found in the quantitative composition of the oils. The plants coming from the optimal, xeric habitat produce oils in which aromatic terpenes (mostly carvacrol) are more abundant, whereas the oils of plants growing in shady and moist sites are mostly composed by acyclic compounds (chiefly geraniol). It seems therefore possible to distinguish two chemical variants of Euphorbia fragifera. The number and kind of pollinating insects have been recorded. Terpenoids from the two kinds of essential oil could be responsible of two different pheromones that attract different kinds of pollinators.

4180439|Starting from the significance of the leaf surface for synmorphology, synecology, herbivory, decomposition and other use values, the leaf shape and size, consistency and seasonality have been surveyed in some forest and nonforested Central European communities. In both the individual species and the plant communities, the leaf size and shape are linearly correlated with mineral nutrient supply and, to some extent, also by soil moisture, both factors having been evaluated according to the importance value for each indicator species. Leaf consistency and periodicity tend to coincide with the moisture gradient. Noteworthy is the smoothing influence of the forest canopy on the representation of various leaf categories in comparison with nonforested communities. No correlation was found between the light factor and the representation of leaf graminoid types.
4179722| Eine neue syntaxonomische Klassifizierung der nitrophilen Gesellschaften ein- bis zweijhriger Arten der Klasse Galio-Urticetea Passarge 67 em. Kopeck 69 wird vorgeschlagen. Sie ermglicht eine Einreihung der Mehrzahl von in der Natur existierenden Gesellschaften in das phytoznologische System, wobei maximale Rcksicht auf ihre innere Dynamik und ihre syngenetische Beziehungen genommen wird. /// Differences in development and distribution of communities of annual and biennial plants belonging to the class Galio-Urticetea are clearly manifested by the various degree of syntaxonomic differentiation of their individual stands. A considerable number of stands encountered in nature cannot be classed within any of the associations described in the sense of Zrich-Montpellier School, and can be classified - according to their species composition - merely within the broad limits of a certain alliance, order, or class. We assume, however, that these stands lacking association rank can also be satisfactorily included in the phytocenological system provided that the syngenetic relations and internal dynamics of the stands are taken into account. The theoretical principles of the syntaxonomic classification used here, together with the general nomenclature of newly defined cenological units, have been explained in detail in an earlier paper (see Kopeck et Hejn 1971). In accordance with this conception, communities of annual and biennial plants which Central European phytocenologists place in the alliance Galio-Alliarion (within Galio-Urticetea), could be classified into units of the following categories: 1. Sociologically saturated associations, i.e. those containing a complete hierarchy of character and differentiating species of the superior syntaxa, including the association character species. 2. Basal communities belonging to no association, i.e. the communities situated within the limits of a class (order, or alliance), and showing a low degree of syntaxonomic differentiation; they consist of the character and differentiating species of higher syntaxa, together with the respective companion species. 3. Derivative communities without any association rank, i.e. communities consisting of character and differentiating species of higher syntaxa (within the limits of the respective class), and furthermore, of companion and character species by which the higher degree of ecological specialization of stands is determined. The ecological and cenological range of species of derivative communities is distinctly wider than that of character species of associations; however, it is narrower than in species of which the basal communities consist. Among the typical character species of derivative communities one encounters plants which have been stimulated - by various human activities - to spread intensively over biotopes of a particular set of cenoses in a certain region, and which have gradually occupied the area (e.g. apophytes and neophytes, such as Torilis japonica, Impatiens parviflora, etc.), while the less competitive native species have been suppressed. 4. The phase of the community is marked by the temporary predominance of a certain species in the stand of the association, both of the basal and derivative communities. It manifests changes in the stand's sociological structure and indicates developmental trends in its syngenesis. Besides various external disturbing factors, the replacing of dominant species in individual community phases is caused mainly by competition. A survey of distinct vegetation units, their brief characterization and species composition are given in Tab. 2-5.

4179543|The meadow plant communities, Arrhenatheretum elatioris alopecuretosum pratensis R. Tx. 1937 and Mesobrometum erecti stipetosum Vicherek 1960, were chosen for investigations of the underground plant parts. Apparent differences in underground dry weight and its seasonal changes in both the communities were observed. The soil environment affects not only the total underground biomass and their changes in time, but also the activity of soil microflora and, consequently, the decomposition rate of dead underground plant parts.
4181388|Populations of Luzula multiflora s.l. in Ireland were examined karyologicall. Plants from 14 populations were invariably tetraploid with 2n=24. Chromosomes of the tetraploid are of AL type (true tetraploidy). Meiosis of the tetraploids is of the same type as described for other Luzula taxa in the literature. In meiosis, 12 bivalents are regularly formed. A hypothesis based on the morphological and allozyme data, that the tetraploids are of alloploid origin, is supported by the present results. Meiosis in an artificial hybrid between the presumed parental taxa, L. campestris and L. pallidula, was studied; a certain tendency towards chromosome doubling was observed. The geographical distribution of the L. multiflora cytotypes is also discussed.

4181471|For many years several taxa belonging to the families Compositae and Rosaceae have been subjected to an intensive research on apomixis. These two families, together with the Gramineae have headed the list of the most thoroughly examined taxonomic groups in this field. At present, new methods are being elaborated and new problems solved within the following genera known to be apomictic, viz. Antennaria, Hieracium, Taraxacum, Alchemilla, Potentilla and Rubus. Many general problems still require more attention in future studies. Seven of them are considered in the present article: 1. frequency of apomixis; 2. occurrence of apospory and diplospory within one taxon; 3. nonfunctional apospory; 4. facultativeness of autonomous apomixis; 5. origin of endosperm; 6. timing of embryo and endosperm development in apomicts; 7. instability of the endosperm type. Both Compositae and Rosaceae produce suitable material for such research projects.
4180054| Die Arbeit beschreibt die synsystematische Stellung und die primren Standortsfaktoren der xerothermen Staudengesellschaften im Wallis und in angrenzender Waadt (Schweizer Zentral-Alpen). Diese Gesellschaften sind als Brachypodio pinnati-Geranion sanguinei Tx. in Mller 1962 em. van Gils et Kozlowska 1977, Brachypodietalia Korneck 1974 und Festuco-Brometea Br.-Bl. et Tx. 1943 klassifiziert. /// We have described the floristic composition and the primary site factors of xerothermic forb meadows and forb fringes (known as Brachypodio-Geranion, Brachypodietalia, Festuco-Brometea) in the Rhone valley in the Swiss Central Alps between Visp and Montreux. Further we have discussed the synsystematic position of these vegetations. The two associations, with their subunits, are distinguishable as follows: (a) the suboceanic Geranio-Trifolietum alpestris Mll. 1962, which only grows locally on silicateous substratum, in Ravoire (Martigny). (b) the intra-alpine Trifolio medii-Laserpitietum latifolii van Gils et Gilissen 1976; in Vaud this association has only been recorded on calcareous substratum, but in the more subcontinental Valais it grows on both calcareous and silicateous soils. The associations just mentioned are restricted to southerly exposed slopes and to altitudes varying between 750-1550 m. The stands at the lowest altitudes (750-950 m) have to be sought in a relatively humid climate (precipitation 1200 mm) or otherwise they are found on deep soils with alternating dry and humid conditions (in German: 'Wechselfeucht'). Characteristicly enough the most elevated relevs have been derived from rubble and heaps of stone in the driest part of the local Brachypodio-Geranion distribution area. Some primary Brachypodio-Geranion stands are noticeable. Most often, however, the Valaisian Brachypodio-Geranion communities have developed as forb fringe alongside present-day meadows, as a forb stadium of abandoned meadows or on road banks. The Brachypodio-Geranion communities are not resistent to intensive pasturing, annual mowing or fertilising. Other anthropogenic influences like burning, chopping of invading arboreous species and mechanical disturbance of the biogeocoenoses can influence the establishment and persistence of the Brachypodio-Geranion positively. As the last feature we have discussed the ecological significance of the polyploidy of the species, which are dominating the Brachypodio-Geranion.

4180795| In a semi-natural, species-rich perennial grassland community (Pulsatillo-Festucetum rupicolae), temporal variation of species composition was studied in permanent plots during secondary succession induced by herbicides selective to dicots and monocots and herbicides of total effect. The effectiveness of using different similarity matrices in detecting vegetation dynamic changes was investigated. Differences caused by treatments in (1), the coenological similarity relations, (2) the direction of secondary succession, (3) the rates of change measured as floristic change (Srensen index) and as change of species cover (Czekanowski's coefficient), (4) the reestablishment of the original state, (5) the seasonal dynamics, (6) the responses to stress situation (drought) have been analysed. The vegetation dynamic processes of the community near stable state were mainly influenced by the differences between years. During the 5 years of study the changes referred to the first sampling date showed a trend induced by changing climatic conditions. In the intact community, seasonal fluctuations can be detected very well. The community rich in species has been proved to be resistant to drought, but resilience referring to its recovery following disturbance was relatively small. After having been drastically disturbed from its dynamically stable state, the grassland community regenerated very slowly. In fact, the community could not recover its original state within five years. The direction and rate of change of the secondary successional and regeneration processes have been determined primarily by the species first occupying the bare ground after herbicide treatment, and the vegetative regeneration of the species present, namely the "competition for space". The main differences between treatments lie in the behaviour of the constituent species in the different coenostates developed following the disturbance.

4179746| Imperatoria ostruthium gehrt im Gebirge Orlick hory (Adlergebirge) zu den allochthonen Arten. Es ist sehr wahrscheinlich, dass sie hier von deutsch sprechenden Ansiedlern anfangs des 17. Jahrhunderts eingefhrt wurde, besonders im Zusammenhang mit der sog. Alpenholzhauer-Kolonisation. Als gezogene und verwildernde Heilpflanze verbreitete sie sich im Bereich der damaligen Holzhauersiedlungen, kleiner Bergwirtschaften sowie in den Siedlungen der weiteren Umgebung von Glas- und Hammerhtten, die im 17. und 18. Jahrhundert, in einigen Fllen noch im 19. Jahrhundert, in Betrieb waren. /// The paper deals with the relation between the settlement history and the distribution of Imperatoria ostruthium L. in the Orlick hory mountains (NE. Bohemia). Imperatoria ostruthium belongs to the allochthonous species in the Orlick hory mountains. Its recent distribution is illustrated in Fig. 1. The continuous settlement process at higher altitutes of the Orlick hory in the main started as late as during the second half of the 16th and especially in the first half of the 17th century. In connection with the enormous development of logging for the use of the Bohemian inland, both in the mountains and in the foothills numerous glassworks were set up, iron ores were mined and iron was produced (see Fig. 2). The stream of German-speaking craftsmen, lumber workers and herdsmen coming predominantly from the former county of Kodzko (Poland) increased. A significant reinforcement of the German immigration into the central part of the mountain range come with the colonization by lumber workers from the Alps. At beginning of the 17th lumber workers from the eastern part of the Krkonoe (Giant Mountains), who originally came from the Alps, were brought to the Orlick hory. The regions influenced by this colonization (see Fig. 2) as well as the environs of glass and iron works which were active through the 17th, 18th and in some cases up to the 19th century, conform conspicuously to the regions of the most intensive accumulation of localities of I. ostruthium. Therefore it may be assumed that this species was introduced into the Orlick hory mountains by German-speaking settlers at the beginning of the 17th century. As a favourite medicinal plant of all-round use it was cultivated in the lumber workers' hamlets, in the settlements around the glass and iron works and round little mountain farmsteads especially in the 17th, 18th, and 19th centuries. It escaped from cultivation and has become a permanent part of the vegetation in the vicinity of both present and former settlement. 
4181183|The present work collects the new names of syntaxa (in the sense of the Code of Phytosociological Nomenclature, Barkman et al. 1986) above subassociation rank found in the literature received by the Library of the Conservatoire Botanique in Geneva. For the year 1990 454 names have been listed. For each one of them, a first appreciation about its validity is given relating to the Code of Nomenclature. 8 names are given in addition to the Index 1987 (Theurillat and Moravec 1990), 9 to the Index 1988 (Theurillat and Moravec 1991) and 4 to Index 1989 (Theurillat and Moravec 1992).
4179967|Studies of the Adjarian flora resulted in a detailed classification of the ergasiophygophytes, based mainly on the degree of their naturalization: (1) The ephemeroergasiophygophytes display unstable naturalization both in artificial and natural habitats, and disappear after only a few growing seasons. (2) The deuteroergasiophygophytes show stable naturalization in anthropogenic habitats. (3) The protoergasiophygophytes are distinguished by uncertain stability of naturalization in natural habitats, and, if firmly naturalized on a certain spot, they lack any tendency to further spreading. (4) The autergasiophygophytes tend to spread in natural habitats. (5) The aggressive ergasiophygophytes transform natural vegetation in new plant communities, and can become dominant species in these communities. New terms, viz. emphemeroxenophytes, protoneophytes, non-aggressive neophytes, slightly aggressive neophytes, and postneophytes with vegetative reproduction have also been introduced to express diverse features of the xenophytes.
4181318|Two new associations belonging to the Salicion silesiacae within the Betulo carpaticae-Alnetea viridis are described. These are disclimax shrub communities dominated by Salix silesiaca at higher altitudes of the Fatra Mts. (Western Carpathians). Synmorphological, synecological, syntaxonomical, syngenetical and synchorological characteristics of the communities are given. Floristic differences between the montane shrub communities in the Western Carpathians and those in the Sudeten Mts. are summarized in a synthetic table.
4181521|A taxonomic revision of the Hieracium alpinum group (sensu Flora Europaea) in the Sudeten Mts., the West and the Ukrainian East Carpathians is provided. Six species are distinguished in the area studied, viz. Hieracium alpinum, H. halleri, H. augusti-bayeri, H. melanocephalum, H. tubulosum, and H. schustleri. H. alpinum occurs throughout the mountain ranges studied, three other taxa are endemic to the Sudeten Mts. (H. melanocephalum, H. tubulosum, H. schustleri), one is confined to the West Carpathians (H. halleri, in addition to the Alps) and one is endemic to the Ukrainian East Carpathians (H. augusti-bayeri). A diploid cytotype (2n=18) was ascertained in H. alpinum from the Ukrainian East Carpathians and the same chromosome number was found for H. augusti-bayeri. An agamospermous mode of reproduction was confirmed for the triploid cytotype of H. alpinum, the triploid H. melanocephalum and H. halleri and the tetraploids H. tubulosum and H. schustleri; the diploid taxa were found to be sexual. Pollen production in diploid taxa is high and pollen grains are homogeneous in size; triploid species, as well as tetraploid H. tubulosum, do not produce pollen; tetraploid H. schustleri has pollen grains of variable size. Data on the ecology and distribution of the species are also given.
4180706|A study was made of the morphological variation in seven population samples of B. glacialis. Data on quantitative and qualitative characters reveal that one of the populations differs considerably from the rest. Observations on geographical distribution show that this species is not endemic to the peaks of Sierra Nevada but far more widely distributed than previously realized. Two varieties of B. glacialis, one of which is new, are described.

Eine von natrlichen Gruppen in dem weitumfassenden Inhalt der Familie Thelypteridaceae stellt die Gruppe von zwei Arten aus dem Umkreis von Thelypteris limbosperma (All.) H. P. Fuchs vor, welche sich von den anderen Gruppen durch die Garnitur der Merkmale von verschiedenen Teilen der Pflanze unterscheidet, am besten durch die Merkmale des Wurzelstockes, der Bltter, der Nervatur, der Spreuschuppen, durch die Stellung der Sporenbehlterhufchen, usw. Die Gattung Oreopteris Holub schliesst nur zwei Arten ein - O. limbosperma (All.) Holub and O. quelpaertensis (Christ) Holub. Bei der Lsung der nomenklatorischen Problematik musste eine grndliche Revision der Gltigkeit des Namens Thelypteris Schmidel 1762 durchgefhrt werden, auf Grund deren der Autor diesen Gattungsnamen als einen gltig verffentlichten anerkennt; zugleich mussten auch die Probleme der Typisierung dieses Gattungsnamens gelst werden. Der Autor neigt zur Typisierung mit der Art Thelypteris palustris Schott und zugleich schlgt er vor, diese Typus-Art des Gattungsnamens Thelypteris Schmidel 1762 zu schtzen. In der Gattung Thelypteris Schmidel 1762 wurde auch eine neue nomenklatorische Kombination vorgeschlagen, und zwar Thelypteris palustris Schott subsp. pubescens (Lawson) Holub fr die Pflanzen dieser Art, die in Nord Amerika vorkommen.

4179427| Lysimachia nemorum ist eine in der Slowakei und in den ganzen Karpaten unregelmssig vorkommende Art; dort ist gleichzeitig auch der Auslufer ihres subatlantischen Areals. Sie ist meistens an die Kammgebiete der ganzen Karpaten, in Buchenwldern, gebunden, vorwiegend ausserhalb von Kalkstein und optimal in Lagen von 550 bis 950 m. . d. M., nur selten hher. Ihre ganze Verbreitung in der Slowakei und in den Karpaten ist wahrscheinlich ein Abbild der klimatischen Bedingungen, die sich hier in der ganzen Formung des Areals widerspiegeln. /// In the region of Slovakia, Lysimachia nemorum is most frequent in the Western Beskyds, the downs of Kysuca and, mainly in the mountain ranges of ergovsk Pohorie, Ondavsk Vrchovina and Nzk Poloniny. Less frequently it appears in the group of Pilsko and Babia Gora, in the mountain ranges of Mal Fatra, Oravsk Magura, Liptovsk Hole, Belansk Tatry, Spisk Magura and Pieniny. In addition, though rare, it is known from the Bl Karpaty and the Velk Fatra and some solitary specimens come from Mal Karpaty, the mountain ranges of Vtnk and Spisk Rudoho. The irregulatity of the distribution is due to the subatlantic character of the total distribution area and to the more continental features of the climatic conditions of the above regions. The same applies to the distribution throughout the Carpathian range. 
4180173| Im Verlauf einiger Jahre wurde die Keimungskologie der Frchte von Dipsacus sylvestris Huds., Dipsacus laciniatus L., Cephalaria transsylvanica (L.) Schrad. ex Roem. et Schult., Virga strigosa (Willd. ex Roem. et Schult.) Holub und Virga pilosa (L.) Hill im Laboratorium und auf einer Versuchsparzelle in Pruhonice studiert. Durch Versuche mit mehreren Fruchtproben wurde festgestellt, dass die Frchte der Arten Dipsacus sylvestris, Dipsacus laciniatus und Cephalaria transsylvanica ohne Samenruhe keimen knnen, whrend die Frchte von Virga strigosa und Virga pilosa ene tiefere Samenruhe durchmachen, die durch den physiologischen Zustand des Keimes verursacht ist. Die Dormanz wurde nur in der Erde oder bei kalter Stratifikation unterbrochen. Weiter wurden bei einzelnen Arten verschiedene Beobachtungen und Versuche ber Phnologie der Keimpflanzen, die Schwimmfhigkeit der Frchte und Disseminationzeit der Frchte durchgefhrt. /// The germination ecology of 5 species of the family Dipsacaceae was investigated over several years. It was found that under favourable conditions Dipsacus sylvestris, Dipsacus laciniatus, and Cephalaria transsylvanica were able to germinate without diapause within various limits of temperatures, while the fruits of Virga strigosa and Virga pilosa passed through a deeper dormancy, which could be interrupted only by cold stratification (betweed +1 and +8 C) for several months. In Virga pilosa, germination started between the 86th and 126th days, and the largest number of fruits germinated between the 4th and 6th months after the beginning of stratification. In Virga strigosa, germination started between the 49th and 103rd days, and the largest number of fruits germinted between the 3rd and 6th months. The deeper dormancy of V. strigosa has already been pointed out (Lhotsk 1968b). All five species under study have a big, well-differentiated embryo in their fruits which fills almost the whole seed and which does not show any further development until the start of germination. In Virga strigosa and V. pilosa dormancy is caused by the physiological state of the embryo. In both species dissemination is tachysporous which contributes favourably to the fact that most seeds are able to overcome the dormancy as early as the next growing season. Kinochory and boleochory are the most important types of dissemination. All species under study can also be distributed by nautochory. The fruits of four species are specifically light. The fruits of Virga strigosa float on water for several hours thanks to the air bublles clinging to their surface. All species (especially Dipsacus sylvestris and D. laciniatus) can also be distributed by endochory, first of all by the birds. The synanthropic species are also distributed by various forms of human activity. 
4180004|The submerged aquatic vascular vegetation was studied in the Finger Lakes and in two bays of Lake Ontario in northern New York State, U.S.A. The species composition, structure and biomass of the communities are related to the principal habitat factors such as trophic status of the lakes, bottom slope and substrate, current and stream effects, and depth. A record of the development of changes in the trophic status of the lakes and in the species composition of their submerged vascular vegetation is outlined. An attempt is made to assess the effects of catastrophic events (floods and cloudbursts in the watershed) on the lake vegetation.
4179909|Data on standing crop of litter, litter production and disappearance in three alluvial meadow plant communities are presented. The influence of ecological conditions and quality of litter on litter decomposition rate, and the chemical changes of litter during decomposition are described.
4180335| Die phytoznologische Variabilitt und die Verbreitung des Aceri-Carpinetum wurden aufgrund von Analyse und Synthese eines umfangreichen Aufnahmenmaterials festgestellt. Das Aceri-Carpinetum umfasst Schuttwlder der Eichen-Hainbuchenwald-Stufe auf das gegliederte Relief der Fluss- und Bachtler gebunden; es ist auf kologisch adquaten Standorten des Hochlandes esk vysoina (Bhmisches Hochland) und des Aussenkarpaten-Systems verbreitet. Diese Assoziation wird in vier Subassoziationen gegliedert, u. zw. Aceri-Carpinetum aegopodietosum, Aceri-Carpinetum aconitetosum vulpariae, Aceri-Carpinetum abietetosum und Aceri-Carpinetum festucetosum altissimae. /// The association Aceri-Carpinetum Klika 1941 represents the edaphically and mesoclimatically conditioned scree woods of the Carpinion belt, occurring mainly on steep, shaded slopes of the narrow river valley of the Bohemian Massif. The tree layer is characterised by a rich and constant occurrence of Acer pseudo-platanus, A. platanoides, Ulmus glabra, Tilia platyphyllos and Fraxinus excelsior. Of the climax trees Carpinus betulus and locally also Quercus petraea and Q. robur grow in this association. Fagus sylvatica occurs occasionally in narrow canyons in which temperature inversion takes place, or on the transition to the submontane beech belt. The herb layer is rich in species and is composed mainly of the Fagetalia character species. The differential species group of the Aceri-Carpinetum versus the Mercuriali-Fraxinetum is composed of Campanula rapunculoides, Stellaria holostea, Galium sylvaticum and Hepatica nobilis. The shrub layer has a very small cover, the moss synusia is distributed only on rocks and stones. The phytosociological variability of the association in various parts of Czechoslovakia (Czech Socialist Republic) is documented by a synoptic table of published sets of relevs (239 relevs) as well as by the author's unpublished relevs (42 relevs). The association is divided into four subassociations. Aceri-Carpinetum aegopodietosum Klika 1941 em. Husov - represents the typical subassociation, which is negatively characterised; the differential species groups of the other subassociations are absent. It is distributed on base rich igneous rocks as well as on crystalline silicate rocks, containing larger quantities of mineral nutrient reserves. The centre of its distribution in Bohemia is in dissected narrow valleys in the hills of the Berounka valley, in Moravia in the hills of Adamovsk vrchovina, especially in the canyon of the river Svitava. The soil of the later developemental steges of this subassociation is mull-like ranker or ranker-braunerde; of the more nature stage, eutrophic braunerde. All these soils usually contain many rocks and stones. The rhizosphere in rich in bases, with very good nitrifying power; the humus formation is favourable. Aceri-Carpinetum aconitetosum vulpariae Husov is confined to the limestones of karst areas; it occurs in esk and Moravsk kras and Pavlovsk vrchy. It is characterised by differential species such as Cornus mas, Berberis vulgaris, Viola mirabilis, Primula veris, Aconitum vulparia, Bupleurum falcatum, B. longifolium, Melittis melissophyllum, Lathyrus niger and Polygonatum odoratum. In the moss layer species confined to calcareous rocks predominate, for instance Anomodon attenuatus, A. viticulosus, Camptothecium lutescens and Cteniduum molluscum. The soil type of this subassociation is young rendsina very rich in humus, having usually high stone and rock content in the A horizon, which increases strongly with depth. These soils are rich in calcium carbonate, and have a good decompostion and humification; the humus form is rendsina mulllike moder. The subassociations described have two geographically conditioned variants: typical variant, which occurs in the hilly land of the Berounka bazin (incl. esk kras) and the variant with Euonymus verrucosa, occurring in the hilly land Brnnsk vrchovina (incl. Moravsk kras) and Pavlovsk vrchy. The variant with Euonymus verrucosa is characterised by a group of Carpathian migrants such as Euonymus verrucosa, Isopyrum thalictroides, Euphorbia amygdaloides, Geranium phaeum and Glechoma hirsuta. Aceri-Carpinetum abietetosum (Mikyka 1952) Husov - occurs on the margin of the distribution area of the Carpinion communities. In warmer habitats the tree layer is dominated by Tilia cordata, in colder and moister ones by T. platyphyllos. Abies alba accedes with a high constancy, Carpinus betulus on the contrary decreases or is entirely absent. This subassociation has been found on silicate crystalline rocks in the narrow upper parts of such river valleys as the Vltava, Lunice, Stela and Orlice. It occupies shady slopes with soils belonging to ranker-braunerde or to a mesotrophic variant of braunerde with high skeleton content. Aceri-Carpinetum festucetosum altissimae Klika 1959 - represents a locally conditioned community, documented by a small number of relevs only. This subassociation prefers valleys with temperature inversion, where it is localized almost entirely on semiconvex to convex parts of shady slopes in silicate soils. Some communities form a transition to submontane beech forests. In the tree layer Fagus sylvatica and Abies alba often grow; the physiognomy of the herb layer is dominated by Festuca altissima. The soils of this subassociation belong to ranker-braunerde or to the mesotrophic variant of the braunerde. The A horizon of these soils is only moderately rich in bases. Aceri-Carpinetum festucetosum altissimae has been found in the hilly land Kivokltsk vrchovina and Beneovsk pahorkatina. 
4179944| Problems of generic names which become nomenclaturally superfluous by inclusion of the type of an earlier generic name are discussed on the basis of the change of Art. 63 of the Code adopted in Leningrad. The author disagrees with the restriction of illegitimity in generic names and discusses briefly some points associated with these questions (breach of horizontal relation of names; violation of relations between taxonomy and nomenclature; violation of the long used principle of superfluity; warranty of the principle of superfluity; competence of the taxonomic approach to the solution of problems of superfluity; scanty knowledge of names of infrageneric taxa; problems of linking basionymic infrageneric names to corresponding generic names; different views on the validity of various types of indirect reference; problems of lectotypification; inconsistencies in the text of the Code). In connection with the preparation of an account of perennial oats for "Flora Europaea" the author was, however, compelled to accept Avenula (Dumort. 1824) Dumort. 1868 instead of Avenochloa Holub 1962; 30 new nomenclatural combinations resulted from this unnecessary change in the Code. /// Der Gegenstand dieses Artikels liegt in der Diskussion der Problematik der berflssigen Gattungsnamen im Zusammenhang mit Art. 63 des Kodes. Ansichten ber die berflssigkeit der Namen entwickelten sich im Laufe der Zeit und vernderten sich von ursprnglich rein taxonomischem Zutritt (bereinstimmende taxonomische Umgrenzung) zur Aufnahme der berflssigkeit, gegrndet auf das Einschliessen des Typus eines frher verffentlichten gltigen Namens. In neuerer Zeit wurde die berflssigkeit der Namen vom Charakter der nomenklatorischen Kombinationen in solchen Fllen beschrnkt, wenn das Epitheton des Basionyms der Kombination legitim war. Diese Ausnahme wurde in Leningrad auch auf die Gattungsnamen und Namen oberhalb des Gattungsniveaus ausgebreitet. Flogerungen dieser Aktion sind bisher nicht bekannt; gem einem konkreten Fall - der erzwungenen Ersetzung des Gattungsnamens Avenochloa durch Avenula, der im Artikel ausfhrlich beschrieben ist, zeigen sich die Ergebnisse eher als negativ. Der Autor stimmt der Einschrnkung der Illegitimitt der berflssigen Namen nicht zu und diskutiert verschiedene Punkte der fraglichen Problematik. Er nimmt als berechtigt an, die Probleme der berflssigkeit von Namen in einzelnen Rangstufen zu lsen, nmlich unterschiedlich bei den horizontalen und bei den vertikalen Verschiebungen. Von 2 nomenklatorischen Typen unter einem Gattungsnamen sollte man den Vorzug dem geben, der in der gegebenen Rangstufe Zeitprioritt aufweist. Das Prinzip der berflssigkeit der Namen geht aus der taxonomischen Seite des Studiums hervor und hat seinen Platz in der nomenklatorischen Praxis schon seit einer langen Zeit; die Beziehung zwischen Taxonomie und Nomenklatur wrde durch seine Aufhebung wesentlich gestrt. Das Unterscheiden von einer nomenklatorischen (homotypischen, obligaten) und einer taxonomischen (heterotypischen, fakultativen) berflssigkeit der Namen ist in der Praxis nicht berechtigt. Die Auffassung der berflssigen Namen als illegitime Namen dauert in der botanischen Nomenklatur seit der Zeit des Einfhrens des Priorittsprinzips an. Neben der Typusmethode sollte fr die Bestimmung der berflssigen Namen als eine ihr gleichwertige Methode auch die Umgrenzungsmethode bentzt werden. Manche Schwierigkeiten knnen vom Fakt folgen, da die Namen der infragenerischen Taxa, die als Basionyme der Gattungsnamen gelten knnen, nur unvollkommen bekannt sind (ihr nomenklatorischer Charakter, Typisierung). Die Verbindung zwischen den infragenerischen Basionymen und den Gattungsnamen kann manchmal auch indirekt sein und unterschiedliche Anschauungen auf die Berechtigkeit der verschiedenen Arten der indirekten Hinweise knnen existieren. Whrend der Lektotypisierung der Gattungsnamen wird es ntig sein, die Problematik von allen Namen der verwandten Taxa (Namen von infragenerischen Taxa inbegriffen) zu bercksichtigen, damit die nderungen von einem rein nomenklatorischen Charakter in der Zukunft vermeiden werden knnten. Im Text des Kodes sollte der Termin "incorrect" definiert werden, wie auch die Umstnde der Vernderung des nicht korrekten Namens zu einem korrekten Namen nher bestimmt werden. In Fllen von taxonomischen Einschrnkungen sollten die Namen der betreffenden Taxa immer in einer emendierten Form angegeben werden. Fr die Lsung der Problematik des Art. 63 sollte eine spezielle Kommission errichtet werden, die die Vorschlge fr den nchsten Kongress vorbereiten sollte. Die nderungen des Kodes sollten immer sehr bedchtig durchgefhrt werden, damit die Namen, die nach dem Wortlaut einer Ausgabe des Kodes vorgeschlagen wurden, nicht in einer kurzen Zeit nach dem Wortlaut der nchsten Ausgabe des Kodes verndert werden mssten; dies gilt hauptschlich fr die Gattungsnamen, nach deren Ersetzungen oft viele nderungen der Artennamen folgen mssen. Aufgrund der nderung des Kodes in Leningrad ist es jetzt ntig, den Namen Avenochloa Holub 1962, der in bereinstimmung mit den Regeln des Kodes vorgeschlagen wurde, durch den Namen Avenula (Dumort.) Dumort. 1868 zu ersetzen, wenn auch der letzte Name taxonomisch mit Helictotrichon Bess. 1827 vollkommen identisch und auch immer nomenklatorisch berflssig ist. Diese nderung ist hier zwar als unberechtigt angenommen, aber in Hinsicht auf die Notwendigkeit der Bearbeitung dieser Gattung fr die "Flora Europaea" (die den Kod in seinem ganzen Umfang streng anerkennt) in einem begrenzten Zeitraum, mu die angefhrte nderung des Gattungsnamens leider angenommen werden. In dem Text des Artikels sind die gegenseitigen Verhltnisse der Gattungsnamen Helictotrichon, Avenula und Avenochloa beschrieben, dann ist die Analyse der Artennamen, die bisher unter dem Gattungsnamen Avenula verffentlicht wurden, durchgefhrt (sie werden von illegitimen Namen jetzt korrekte Namen) wie auch die Vorschlge von neuen nomenklatorischen Kombinationen gegeben (1 fr Untergattung, 2 fr Sektionen, 23 fr Arten und 4 fr Unterarten). 4181558| Several textbooks of phytocoenology (plant sociology) are compared. There seems to be a basic difference between Russian and Central European authors. The Russian authors (Naumova, Rabotnov) devote substantial parts of their textbooks to functional elements of communities (populations and consortias) and to their interactions. On the other hand, the Central European authors (Dieren, Dierschke, Moravec) devote a lot of space to methodology of community description. They deal with classification, syntaxonomy and mapping; their view of communities as units enables them to treat the relation to habitat factors extensively. 
4179544| In der vorgelegten Arbeit wird die syntaxonomische Problematik der natrlichen und naturnahen nitrophilen Saumgesellschaften der Verbnde Convolvulion sepium Tx. ex Oberd. 49 und Petasition officinalis Sillinger 33 em. Kopeck hoc loco gelst. Die znologische Charakteristik beider Verbnde erforderte bestimmte nderungen in der Abgrenzung der bergeordneten Vegetationseinheiten: Die Aufteilung der ursprnglichen Klasse Artemisietea vulgaris Lohm., Prsg. et Tx. 50 ist unvermeidlich. Grs 66 in die Klasse Artemisietea vulgaris eingereiht wurden, sind neu in die gengend abgegrenzte Klasse Galio-Urticetea Passarge 67 em. Kopeck hoc loco eingegliedert. Kopeck hoc loco, das karpatische Petasitetum officinalis-glabrati Sillinger 33 und das Petasito-Telekietum speciosae Morariu 67, das ausschliesslich in den ostslowakischen, ostpolnischen, sowjetischen und rumnischen Karpaten verbreitet ist. /// The nitrophilous marginal communities (German term "Saumgesellschaften") treated in the present paper are placed in the alliances Convolvulion sepium Tx. ex Oberd. 49 and Petasition officinalis Sillinger 33 em. Kopeck hoc loco. The Czechoslovak natural communities of the alliance Convolvulion sepium are determined by the following character species: Convolvulus sepium (opt.), Cuscuta europaea (opt.), Cuscuta lupuliformis, Cucubalus baccifer, Senecio fluviatilis, (Galega officinalis). In the Czechoslovakia, there occurs only one association: Cuscuto-Convolvuletum sepium Tx. 47 em. Kopeck hoc loco. It contains two subassociations: 1. the Northwest-Central European subass. Cuscuto-Convolvuletum sepium typicum and 2. the Southeast-European subass. Cuscuto-Convolvuletum sepium aristolochietosum. The communities Petasition officinalis Sillinger 33 em. The third association of the alliance, Petasito-Telekietum speciosae Morariu 67, occurs in Czechoslovakia only in the East-Slovakian Carpathians. The place of the units described in the recent phytocenological system: The splitting of the class Artemisietea vulgaris Lohm., Prsg. et Tx. 50 seems to be necessary and correct. According to the original description this class includes the group of ruderal communities occurring at dry and intensively insolated habitats (order Onopordetalia Br.-Bl. et Tx. 43 em. Grs 66) and the groups of nitrophilous communities growing at moist to fresh, shady to insolated habitats. The present paper transfers these last-mentioned community-units to the class Galio-Urticetea Passarge 67 em. Kopeck hoc loco. According to the systematic arrangement suggested here (see page 250), this class includes two groups: A. The group of natural to semi-natural marginal communities with the orders Convolvuletalia sepium Tx. 50 (with the alliance Convolvulion sepium) and [(?) Circaeo-Stachyetalia Passarge 67] and Petasito-Chaerophylletalia Morariu 67 (with the alliance Petasition officinalis); - B. The group of ruderal to semi-ruderal nitrophilous substitute communities which are identical with the new defined order Lamio (albi) - Chenopodietalia (boni-henrici). 
4179439| The paper presents the results of pollen analyses of samples collected from two peat localities in the Orlick hory mountains in Czechoslovakia. 4181412|Why some plants are damaged by flooding and others are not, is not a question that can be answered by citing any one particular mechanism or sequence of events. Flood-tolerant plants like obligate aquatic species can survive inundation but differ in that they are also adapted to withstand the consequences of becoming unflooded. Flooding implies a transitory state so that when water tables drop, adapted species have to be able to survive being deprived of the physical support of flood-water as well as re-exposure to a normal air supply. A review of flooding tolerance mechanisms reveals that tolerant species combine a range of adaptations which, depending on the life strategy of the species, can play different roles in enabling intact plants to adjust to both rising and falling water levels. Flooding is also a seasonal stress with many temperate plant communities being subjected to high water tables in winter. The mechanisms that confer tolerance of winter flooding also differ from those that allow plants to grow when flooded during the growing season. This review argues therefore, that reductionist investigations, which examine isolated organs or individual processes, may not be the most suitable method to apply to understanding the complexity of reactions that are needed to survive flooding. Instead, a holistic approach is advocated which examines the reactions of whole plants to changing water levels at different seasons of the year.

Ihre Bestnde sind optimal auf lehmsandigen rezenten Anschwemmungen der Karpatenbche und Quellrinnen (semimerse bis demerse Uferkotope des stenosaleutischen Ufertyps) entwickelt. /// The new association of the alliance Sparganio-Glycerion Br.-Bl. et Sissingh apud Boer 1942, the Glycerietum nemoralis-plicatae ass. nova, is distributed in the montane and submontane zones of the Czechoslovak West Carpathians. 4179974| Die submontanen krautreichen Buchenwlder auf Silikatbden in der westlichen Tschechoslowakei (Tschechische Sozialistische Republik) zerfallen in vier Assoziationen: 1. Matuszkiewicz 1960 an. Die Zusammensetzung der Assoziationen ist durch pflanzensoziologische Tabellen belegt und ihre Verbreitung auf einer Punktkarte erfasst. /// The submontane herb-rich beech forests (or lime-beech or fir-beech forests) on silicate soils in western Czechoslovakia (Czech Socialist Republic) split into four associations: 1. Tilio cordatae-Fagetum Mrz 1960 em. Moravec 1977 - this association comprises the submontane herb-rich beech, lime-beech, or fir-beech forests of central, western and southern Bohemia. They formed (or still form where preserved) the climax vegetation on silicate soils in the submontane belt of lower highlands in the above area. Fagus sylvatica predominates in the tree layer accompanied irregularly by Carpinus betulus. Tilia cordata, Quercus petraea or Abies alba (recently retreating). The herb layer consists mainly of the Fagetalia character species, the Fagion species are less numerous (Dentaria bultifera, Actaea spicata, Prenanthes purpurea). The differential species group compared with other beech forest associations is composed of Zerna benekenii, Cardamine impatiens, Vicia sylvatica and Campanula trachelium. The species composition of this association in individual territories is documented in synoptic tables of the published sets of relevs (49 relevs) and in relev tables with 35 author's relevs. The Tilio cordatae-Fagetum occurred (or still occurs) in larger or smaller islands either on higher elevations as the climax community conditioned macroclimatically or on slopes of northern orientation conditioned microclimatically. It seldom occurs as the subclimax on steep slopes with ranker-braunerde. This association has been found in Bohemia only, in the hilly land Stedoesk pahorkatina, in the hilly land Vrchovina Berounky, on the ridge Lovsk prh and on the northern border of the Doupovsk hory Mts. It is concentrated between 400 and 600 m and shows a significant preference for slopes of northern orientation. The Tilio cordatae-Fagetum occupies waste mantle of the Pleistocene age on silicate rocks of various trophic degree (except those poor in bases) where soils belonging to the Centro-European braunerde (mainly to the mesotrophic variant) developed. 2. Tilio platyphylli-Fagetum Klika 1939 - represents a locally conditioned association which occurs on volcanic hills in the western part of the esk stedoho Mts. The tree layer is composed of four species on the average - Fagus sylvatica predominates Tilia platyphyllos, Quercus petraea and Tilia cordata are mixed in. The shrub layer is fairly regularly present, however, with a low cover degree; it is composed primarily of Lonicera xylosteum, Daphne mezereum and Ribes uva-crispa. In the herb layer the Fagetalia species mostly participate. The Fagion species are also quite numerous (Actaea spicata, Hordelymus europaeus, Prenanthes purpurea); they meet with some character species of the Carpinion (Stellaria holostea, Galium sylvaticum). Tilia platyphyllos, Lonicera xylosteum, Stellaria holostea, Galium sylvaticum and Convallaria majalis, can be considered the differential species compared with other beech forest associations. The species composition of this association is documented by synoptic tables of the published sets of relevs (16 relevs) and by 8 author's relevs. The Tilio platyphylli-Fagetum occurs in small islands in microclimatically favoured sites within a Carpinion territory with complicated geology and varied countryside. This is reflected also in the species composition; the coppice management of the stands probably contributed to enrichment in thermo- or heliophilous species. 3. Melico-Fagetum Seibert 1954 - encompasses Melica uniflora dominated beech forests which settled or still settle silicate soils in the submontane belt of northern to eastern Bohemia and northern and central Moravia as climax communities. The tree layer is dominated by Fagus sylvatica to which Acer pseudoplatanus, Carpinus batulus, rarely Abies alba (recently retreating) and Ulmus glabra admix with a lower constancy. The herb layer is characterized by a lower species number and by a predominance of Melica uniflora. It is composed mainly of the Fagetalia species, the Fagion species are less represented (Dentaria bulbifera, Festuca altissima, Hordelymus europaeus). The species composition of the association in western Czechoslovakia is documented by 14 author's relevs; some individual relevs have been published from northern and eastern Bohemia only. The Melico-Fagetum has been found in the Luick hory Mts., in the hilly land Ralsk vrchovina, in the mountains Nzk Jesenk and Odersk vrchy and in the highland Drahansk vrchovina. It occurs as a climax community primarily at altitudes of 400 to 600 m (seldom higher) and prefers deeper soils of the meso- to oligotrophic Centro-European braunerde on a flat senile relief showing no preference for a certain exposure. On the steeper volcanic hills. in northern Bohemia the association forms small islands confined to deeper weathered soils. 4. Carici pilosae-Fagetum Oberdorfer 1957 - in western Czechoslovakia this represents an association of herb-rich climax beech forests on silicate soils in the submontane belt of the western Carpathians. The tree layer consists almost solely of deciduous trees among which Fagus sylvatica predominates accompanied constantly by Quercus petraea. The herb layer is not too rich in species; in its species composition the Fagetalia species predominate in number whereas of the Fagion only Dentaria bulbifera achieves a higher constancy. Carex pilosa (dominant), Cephalanthera longifolia and Tithymalus amygdaloides can be considered the differential species compared with other beech forest associations. This association has not hitherto been published from Czechoslovakia. It is documented by 29 relevs 24 of which are new. The Carici pilosae-Fagetum has been found already exclusively in the Carpathians; as an exception it penetrates into the southeastern margin of the highland Drahansk vrchovina. This association does not occur in Bohemia. In the Moravian Carpathians the Carici pilosae-Fagetum has been attested in the highland Chiby, in the Bl Karpaty Mts. and in the hill group of Malenk. It occurs mainly at altitudes between 400 and 600 m of various exposure; in lower altitudes it descends into northern slopes. This association occupies mild slopes or flat ridges with deep soils belonging to the Centro-European braunerde (mostly to the mesotrophic variant). 5. A more detail comparison of some herb-rich beech forests occurring in submontane sites has shown their appurtenance to the Dentario enneaphylli-Fagetum Oberdorfer ex W. et A. Matuszkiewicz 1960. The beech forests under consideration occur in the hilly land near Jevany (Central Bohemia) and in the elezn hory Mts. 
4180315| A cytogeographical and morphological (fruit-types and leaf-shape) study of the critical Rumex acetosella aggregate has been made on the basis of 38 population samples, for the most part from the Czech Socialistic Republic. In the genecological respect the populations from Bohemia and those from North and West Moravia fit into the pattern earlier found in West and Central Europe (i.e. they are 6, mainly angiocarpous, and have non-dissected leaf lobes). Samples from the xerothermic region of South Moravia and parts of Slovakia and adjacent Austria are thought to be related to the Balkan population group (mainly 4, gymnocarpous and with much dissected - multifid - leaf lobes). Evidence of introgressive hybridisation from the 4 into the 6 ploidy-level has been found in the region of the well known migration route through the Moravian Gate.

4181306|The interactions between field layer vascular plants and Sphagnum mosses in peat-forming systems are discussed in terms of differences in growth strategies, access to light, acquisition of mineral nutrients and water and the processes involved in the formation of the micro-topographical structures characteristic for these systems. To keep pace with the vertical growth of Sphagnum, the co-occurring vascular plants require a growth strategy involving continuous movement of the growing point and meristematic tissue upwards and a frequent formation of adventitious roots. The growth form and architecture of the vascular plants determine the occurrence and distribution of the structural units on a mire, the hummocks, lawns and hollows. Dwarf shrubs and other vascular plants with an orthotropic growth pattern characterise hummocks, where they form a firm matrix which reinforces and supports the spongy biomass of Sphagnum. In a similar way, clonal herbs stabilise the lawns because of the predominantly plagiotropic, or only weakly orthotropic, growth pattern of the rhizomes and coarse roots in the upper, oxic layers. Extended periods of drought often may have deleterious effects on the mosses but smaller impacts on the vascular plants because of their more efficient water conducting system. Different sources of mineral nutrients are used by Sphagnum (atmospheric deposition) and the vascular plants (mineralisation of the organic matter). The presence of Sphagnum, therefore, reduces the supply of nutrient resources to the vascular plants. Sphagnum thereby gains a competitive advantage. A high rate of mineralisation would be beneficial to the vascular plants by increasing their growth rates causing shading of the Sphagnum mosses and covering the moss layer by the above-ground litter fall. However, the slow decomposition of Sphagnum litter keeps the system in balance as it will reduce the nutrient supply to the vascular plants.

4181118| Use of morphological, karyological and enzymatic approaches in the study of 11 populations of Phragmites australis (Cav.) Trin. ex Steud. originating from different geographic areas, climates and ecological conditions reveals a spatial differentiation of populations. 25130306|Pollen of 110 species from 18 genera in the Portulacaceae has been examined by light and scanning electron microscopy, and a representative number by transmission electron microscopy. Three basic pollen types were found: 3-colpate with thick tectum and foot layer with prominent unbranched columellae and an extremely thin endexine; pantoporate with thick tectum and foot layer with branched columellae enclosing pores and an endexine that is one to two layers thick; pantocolpate with thin tectum and foot layer with broad, short unbranched columellae and an inconspicuous endexine. All pollen types, however, have a spinulose and tubuliferous/punctate ektexine. Also, all the genera except three, Calandrinia H.B.K., Montia L. and Talinum Adanson are stenopalynous. There is, however, no absolute correlation between pollen morphology and geographical distribution, although both the major centre of palynological diversity and the majority of all species with tricolpate grains occur in South America.

4180607|Successional stages of the xeric series of old-fields in the Bohemian Karst have been studied from the point of view of disturbance of plant communities by different intensities of mowing. Changes of biomass, diversity and population structure have been examined. The communities of younger successional stages are relatively more disturbed but they are able to reestablish themselves rather quickly. The communities of the older stages are characterized by a slower rate of recovery. The stability of younger stages may be understood as resilience and stability of older stages as resistance.
4180678| Six new genera are designated for the predominantly foliicolous species with hyaline, septate ascospores originally included in the artificial genera Bacidia, Catillaria and Lopadium. These are Fellhanera gen. n. which, on the basis of ascus structure, belongs to the family Pilocarpaceae and includes 19 species, as well as Badimia gen. n. (6 species), Barubria gen. n. (1 species), Loflammia gen. n. (3 species), Calopadia gen. n. (6 species) and Logilvia gen. n. (1 species) which with the previously described genera Lasioloma R. Sant. and Tapellaria Mll. Arg. em. R. Sant. are classified in the family Ectolechiaceae as they are related to Sporopodium Mont. The campylidia, special reproductive organs of the lichens concerned, are present in all members of the family. They are considered to be phylogenetically derived from apothecia. The conidia they produce vary in shape and structure and can be divided into different types, each of which is characteristic of a particular genus. The necessary new combinations are introduced in an appendix. /// Die vorliegende Arbeit befasst sich mit der Systematik der berwiegend foliicolen Arten der Sammelgattungen Catillaria, Bacidia und Lopadium, die sich durch paraplectenchymatisch gebaute Excipula, relativ dnne, einfache bis reich verzweigte und netzartig verbundene Paraphysen, keulige Asci mit J+ blauem Tholi und septierte hyaline Ascosporen auszeichnen; fr sie wurde schon frher eine neue Gattung Lobaca ad interim vorgeschlagen (Vzda 1983). 4180358|Misra et Misra (1981) have concluded, on the basis of an analysis of a grassland community, that there is significant negative correlation between species diversity and dominance indices. It is shown that this result is an unfortunate misunderstanding because negative correlation is an inevitable consequence of indices definitions. Some other shortcomings concerning diversity, stability and species-abundance distributions, contained in the paper, are pointed out.

4181426|During the last few years alder has declined in South Bohemia. The possible role of mycorrhizal and actinorhizal symbioses is reviewed and some of the preliminary results from experiments testing the influence of these symbioses on alder growth and the influence of eutrophication on the development of these symbioses are reported. Seedlings of Alnus glutinosa were inoculated with arbuscular mycorrhizal (AM) fungi and the actinomycete Frankia in experiment 1, and with rhizosphere soil collected from field sites with different degrees of alder damage in experiment 2. In both experiments, a solution containing nitrate, ammonia and phosphorus in concentrations simulating eutrophic waters, was applied. Both symbioses markedly promoted the growth of the seedlings in experiment 1. The plants inoculated with the rhizosphere soil microflora in experiment 2 were larger than the control plants. Response of the seedlings to the inoculation with the soil from the rhizosphere of damaged alder trees from six field sites differs, even though no correlation was found relating growth to the health status of the trees. Nutrient treatment did not have any effect on the growth of seedlings in either experiment. The dry weight of Frankia was greater in mycorrhizal plants compared to nonmycorrhizal plants and mycorrhizal colonization is reduced in Frankia inoculated plants supplemented with phosphorus in experiment 1. Nitrogen enhanced mycorrhizal colonization in nodulated plants which were not supplemented with phosphorus no effect of nitrogen on actinorhiza was observed.

4181417|This paper shows the effect of re-aeration following hypoxic pretreatment on the glutathione system in plants with different flooding tolerance. Re-aeration of hypoxically pretreated roots led to an increase of TBA-rm content indicating an accelerated lipid peroxidation (post-anoxic injury). Re-admission of oxygen resulted in a clear increase in the content of total glutathione in both flooding-intolerant species Myosotis arvensis and Senecio jacobaea. Simultaneously, the high ratio between reduced (GSH) and oxidized (GSSG) glutathione decreased in these species upon the onset of re-aeration, while the tolerant Myosotis palustris and Senecio aquaticus showed only little changes in contents of GSH and GSSG. An imbalance in GSH/GSSG ratio reflects oxidative stress. The glutathione reductase (GR) reacted very differently in the investigated genera. The metabolic response to varying oxygen pressure is much stronger in the flooding-intolerant species compared to species naturally growing in wetlands. The present results suggest that glutathione system is an important component in overcoming oxidative stress.

4180636|Alases are unique grassland landscapes in Central Yacutia, their development influenced by extra-continental arid climate. Twenty three associations have been distinguished and described. These associations form an ecological series from steppe with Festuca lenensis and Stipa krylovii through salt and swamp meadow (Hordeum brevisubulatum, Puccinellia tenuiflora, Alopecurus arundinaceus, Calamagrostis langsdorffii, Carex juncella) to swamp communities of Scolochloa festucacea, Glyceria triflora, Scirpus lacustris and Typha latifolia. The community complexes of specific elements of alas landscapes - baidjerakhs and bulgunnyakhs - are analysed.
4181249| Allozyme techniques, karyotype analyses and cultivation experiments were carried out on 20 population samples of Taraxacum sect. Piesis (Compositae), viz. T. bessarabicum (17 samples from W. and C. Europe, Ukraine and Crimea, Central Asia and the Altai), T. salsum from Crimea, T.  mesohalobium from Crimea, and T. stenolepium from the Caucasus. The taxa studied share a primitive, symmetrical karyotype. All taxa studied are sexual, T. bessarabicum mostly autogamous. Sexuality at the tetraploid level (T. stenolepium) and occasional male sterility in a sexual (T. bessarabicum in Moravia) were recorded for the first time in the genus. Selfing, diploidy and the highly predictable habitat may account for the mostly low level within population allozyme variation in T. bessarabicum. W. and C. European samples of T. bessarabicum are almost invariable allozymically and, as a group, have no unique alleles. The Crimean and Asian group of populations shows higher levels of allozyme variation and has 15 alleles not found in the former group at 13 loci studied. Recent migration from one source region is suggested to account for the homogeneity of the western group, refugial persistence of alleles and possible introgression from sympatric species may have resulted in allele richness in the eastern group. Hybridization between T. bessarabicum and T. salsum was documented by allozyme patterns in a few plants in Crimea. Some aberrant allozyme or karyotypic features of two populations are discussed as well.

4181419|This contribution combines field observation with the literature to argue that stabilised water levels are contributing to reed decline through a lack of vegetative and generative reproduction, and that eutrophic conditions exacerbate this situation. The focus on what causes reed shoots to die has increased our knowledge of what limits the distribution of reed without necessarily increasing our understanding of reed decline. This raises the question as to whether reed beds are in fact dying, or whether reed decline is observable only in the absence of regeneration. The distribution pattern and life-history of reed suggests that generative reproduction is lacking. It is proposed that the temporal scale at which seedling establishment takes place is similar to the time-frame of observed reed decline (10-50 years). As an "encompassing" factor, water regime influences many of the specific factors under investigation. Its role is therefore consistent with agreement in the literature that reed decline is caused by combinations of factors.
4179821|Progenies of triploid and diploid hybrids of tetraploid Arabis hirsuta (L.) Scop. s. str. and diploid A. sagittata (Bertol.) DC. and A. planisiliqua (Pers.) Reichenb. were studied. The observations concerned morphology, cytology, sterility degree of plants and embryological backgrounds. The evolutionary consequences of breakage of the sterility barriers within the complex connected with well pronouced morphological and karyological variability of hybrids are discussed.
4179679|The investigations of growth rhythm, dry matter production, leaf area development and root/shoot ratio of dominant reed bed species, grown in a greenhouse in hydroponic cultures during winter and spring are described. Data on air temperature, relative humidity and density of incoming solar radiation were recorded during the whole season. All species planted in autumn (in a warm greenhouse) presented a pronounced thermoperiodism, i.e. weak growth caused by an incomplete period of dormancy. The winter-planted specimens developed into normal and vigorous plants. The R/S ratio may be a relatively constant characteristic of species, but only for a given growth phase.

4180762| The origin, age and development of a mire deposit in the locality of the Mokr Louky meadows near Tebo were ascertained by means of palaeoecological methods. The first minerogenic sediments originated in a depression at the turn of the Late-Glacial and the Holocene Periods. In the course of minerogenic sedimentation, the vegetational cover was formed by stands of Filipendula. In the middle of the Pre-Boreal Period, the first organic sediments formed by reed plant communities were deposited in the area. In the course of the following periods, plant communities of mire and marshy meadows belonging to the associations of the class Scheuchzerio-Caricetea fuscae predominated on the site. Stands of willow and alder trees were formed in some parts of the deposit most probably towards the end of the Atlantic Period, with their maximum development in the Sub-Boreal to Upper Sub-Atlantic Periods. Pollen analysis produced a more precise foundation for reconstructing the forest vegetation in the centre of the Tbosk pnev Basin. A higher presence of Quercus and a lower one of Fagus, as compared with the results of previous pollen analyses from the borders of the Basin, were ascertained. The palaeoecological analyses are supported by radiocarbon datings. /// Das Alter des Lagers Mokr Louky bei Tebo wurde pollenanalytisch auf die Scheide des Sptglazials und Holozns bestimmt. 4181217| Natural and semi-natural plant communities of Svjatoj Nos Peninsula on the East coast of Lake Baikal, Eastern Siberia, Russia, are classified and described using the methods of Braun-Blanquet phytosociology. A total of 48 associations and communities were recognized, comprising alpine tundra, subalpine forb vegetation, aquatic macrophyte vegetation, tall-herb and poor fens, mires, bogs, meadows, sand-dune and steppe vegetation. Twenty six syntaxa of ranks ranging from subassociation to class are described or validated for the first time. All communities are documented by phytosociological relevs.

Sie ist hier an die submontane und montane Hhestufe gebunden, wo Granit und kristalline Schiefer die geologische Unterlage bilden. Optimale Bedingungen fr die Entwicklung des Polygono-Cirsietum heterophylli bieten jene Standorte, wo wenigstens zu Beginn der Vegetationsperiode das nicht stagnierende Grundwasser in den Rhizosphrenbereich eingreift. Der Boden ist mit Phosphor und Kalium gut versorgt und zeigt oft eine mssig gute Pufferung. Vom pflanzensoziologischen Standpunkt aus weist die Assoziation Beziehungen zu den Gesellschaften des Calthion-Verbandes auf. /// The Polygono-Cirsietum heterophylli, a new association of the order Molinietalia, provisionally classed within the alliance Calthion, is described. The association is mostly found in the montane belt (600 to 900 m alt.) of mountain ranges composed of granite or crystalline rocks. So far, it has been studied in Czechoslovak mountains, namely in the Krun Hory Mts., Slavkovsk Les Mts., Krkonoe Mts. and d'rsk Vrchy Mts; it has also been reported from the Smriny Mts. and Doupovsk Hory Mts. In NW Bohemia, a region under the influence of the oceanic climate, the Polygono-Cirsietum heterophylli descends to the foothills (down to 400 m) while in the Krkonoe Mts., situated further to the eastern continental part of Europe, this association has also been recorded near the lower limits of the subalpine belt (at 1030 m alt.). It occurs around springs over the mountain slopes, and along streams in the valleys. In the latter habitats, the substrate is, as a rule, saturated with percolating water (continuously stagnant underground water is absent). Both kinds of habitats are relatively well supplied with both potassium and phosphorus. From the systematical point of view, three subassociations are distinguished within the association: Polygono-Cirsietum heterophylli typicum, trisetetosum flavescentis and geranietosum silvatici. The latter is differentiated into two geographical races distinguished by the presence of either Phyteuma nigrum or Phyteuma spicatum. Syngenetical relationships of the association to other plant communities of the alliance Calthion, and to those of the alliances Polygono-Trisetion or Violion caninae, are apparent from a key attached to Tab. 1 (p. 62 - 63).

4181267|The growth dynamics of shoot populations and the mode of competition between intra-clonal shoots of two rhizomatous species, Polygonum cuspidatum and Polygonum weyrichii, were investigated at the Houei crater (c. 2380 m a.s.l.) of Mt. Fuji. Three genetic individuals of P. cuspidatum (large, medium and small) and five genetic individuals of P. weyrichii were selected for this research. The growth dynamics of shoot populations were analysed using the diffusion model. In P. cuspidatum, linear G(t,x) functions (mean of absolute growth rates of shoots of size x at time t in the diffusion model) with positive slopes were found in terms of shoot weight in three genetic individuals. The linear G(t,x) functions suggest that smaller-sized shoots were supported by means of physiological integration and not suppressed by larger-sized shoots. As in other clonal plant species, size-independent D(t,x) functions (variance of absolute growth rates of shoots of size x at time t in the diffusion model) were found in P. cuspidatum.
