Jede Assoziation ist mit Vegetationsaufnahmen und der Synonymik belegt und ihre charakteristische Artenkombination, Artenzusammensetzung und Struktur, ihre syngenetischen und topographischen Beziehungen werden beschrieben und ein Vergleich mit der Literatur ist durchgefhrt. /// Xerothermic herbaceous vegetation on volcanic rocks of the eastern part of the esk Stedoho Hills, belongs to the class Festuco-Brometea Br.-Bl. et Tx. 1943. The southern, southwestern and southeastern slopes bear plant communities of the order Festucetalia valesiacae Br.-Bl. et Tx. 1943, within which two alliances and eight associations have been distinguished. The alliance Alysso-Festucion pallentis Moravec 1967 is represented by species-rich petricolous communities growing in shallow A - C soils developed on ledges and in crevices formed by weathering or disintegration of the parent rock, or spread over very steep slopes affected by heavy soil erosion. Plant communities of this alliance belong to the following five associations: 1. Alysso saxatilis-Festucetum duriusculae Klika ex eovsk 1949 (community of steep rock faces in warm regions and along the river valleys); 2. Asperulo glaucae-Festucetum duriusculae Preis in Klika 1939 (open community covering rock ledges and plateaux of basalt hills); 3. Allio montani-Sedetum albi Klika 1939 (initial petricolous community preparing suitable conditions for further succession of more advanced communities of the alliance Alysso-Festucion pallentis and Festucion valesiacae); 4. Melico transsilvanicae-Sempervivetum soboliferi Preis in Klika 1939 (community of grasses, succulent plants, ferns, and therophytes inhabiting continuous rock faces and plateaux); 5. Alysso montani-Potentilletum arenariae Preis 1939 (community developed in a typical form over mild slopes of basic rocks; wide rock and slightly inclined ledges). The alliance Festucion valesiacae Klika 1931 is represented by species-rich herbaceous communities of rocky slopes, distributed mainly over nutrient-rich and more developed A - C soil. Plant communities of this alliance belong to three associations: 1. Carici humilis-Festucetum sulcatae Klika 1951 (communities spread over slopes with soil of variable depth and without dramatic fluctuations of soil moisture in the course of the growing season); 2. Erysimo crepidifolii-Festucetum valesiacae Klika 1933 (open community inhabiting rocky biotopes with shallow but continuous A - C soil); 3. Festuco valesiacae-Stipetum capillatae Sillinger 1931 (community of basic rocks or on loess deep soils; with regard to the succession it belongs to the most advanced communities of the Festucion valesiacae in the esk Stedoho Hills). In agreement with the current development of the phytocoenological nomenclature, the correct name for each syntaxon according to the priority rule is established. All associations are documented by phytocoenological relevs, and relevant synonyms; and their brief characteristic, syngenetical and topographical relationships, and comparison with published data are given. All associations have also been completed by ecological features which will be described in the second part of this paper.

4179968| Cytological and morphological studies have been carried out on populations of Campanula rotundifolia L., C. Tatrae Borbs (group Vulgares) and C. bohemica Hruby (group Scheuchzerianae) from a wide range of habitats in Czechoslovakia. Chromosome counts have been made on material from 185 populations, revealing the presence of two ploidy levels within the limits of the species C. rotundifolia L.: diploid (2n = 34) and tetraploid (2n = 68). Tatrae, subsp. mentiens (Witas.) Kovanda and subsp. sudetica (Hruby) Kovanda], each representing a major regional facies of the species. Within C. bohemica Hruby, two vicarious subspecies are recognized which can be equated with subsp. bohemica and subsp. gelida Kovanda. 4179575| Aus dem Andesitgebiet des Kremnitzer Gebirges (Mittelslowakei) wird eine vegetations-kundliche Analyse der wichtigsten Weidegesellschaften dargelegt. Die Talweiden stellt die Assoziation Lolio-Cynosuretum Tx. 1933 dar. Sie ist nur wenig verbreitet u. zw. in der Subassoziation typicum. Eine hnliche Gesellschaft wird in der Form einer Sammeltabelle aus dem Tal des Slan-Flusses angefhrt. Am meisten sind die Bergweiden verbreitet, die durch die Assoziation Anthoxantho-Agrostietum Sillinger 1933 em. Jurko 1969 reprsentiert werden. Die fr niedrigere Lagen charakteristische Subassoziation A.-A. typicum kann in zwei Varianten gegliedert werden, eine oligotrophe mit Ononis spinosa und eine eutrophe (gemht und beweidet) mit Rhinanthus minor. Die Subassoziation A.-A. nardetosum subass. nova ist in Hhen von ber 700 m anzutreffen. Die bisher verffentlichten Tabellen dieses Typs wurden einer syntaxonomischen Revision unterzogen und im Rahmen dieser Subassoziation mehrere Varianten herausgestellt. Die selteneren Halbtrockenrasen im Kremnitzer Gebirge werden provisorisch nur als Brachypodium pinnatum-Gesellschaft dargestellt. In zwei Aufnahmen aus diesem Gebiet wird das Nardetum montanum Sillinger 1933 dokumentiert. Endlich wird ganz kurz eine wirtschaftliche Bewertung dieser Gesellschaften angefhrt. /// Next to forest, pasture communities constitute the dominant vegetation of the Kremnica Mountains in central Slovakia. They occur principally on mineral-rich andesite soils. In these narrow valleys conditions for extension of the alluvial grasslands represented by the association Lolio-Cynosuretum Txen 1937 are absent. From the point of view of land utilisation they are of high quality but are less extensively farmed than the other pastures of this region. Transitional syntaxa to mountain pastures have not been observed. Reference is made to a similar community from the alluvium of the Slan river as a variant of Poa trivialis. Most of the pastures in the study area, which overlies different geological bedrocks, belong to the regional association Anthoxantho-Agrostietum Sillinger 1933 em. Jurko 1969. On lowlying sites a sub-association A.-A. typicum Jurko 1969 occurs with two variants. The oligotrophic variant with Ononis spinosa is more xero- and thermophilous, while the variant with Rhinanthus minor is widespread in medium and higher situations where it often merges into sub-associations with Nardus stricta. The sub-association A.-A. nardetosum subass. nova spreads on sites up to 700 m above sea level. Formerly, similar communities have been described from Slovakia under different names. After syntaxonomical re-evaluation the author is of the opinion that they can be included in this sub-association. The differential species indicate a connecting link to the alliance Nardo-Agrostidion. Within this sub-association several new variants can be distinguished. These are, variant with Genista pilosa (Dostl 1933); variant with Viola tricolor ssp. subalpina (Sillinger 1933, Svoboda 1939); variant with Cytisus procumbens (Mikyka 1932); variant with Succisa pratensis (Mth et Kovcs 1960); and variant with Filipendula vulgaris (Fajmonov 1963). Mesoxerophytic pastures occur less frequently and only as small areas on both calcareous and andesitic soils. Owing to the lack of phytocoenological data from Slovakia it has not been possible to determine these precisely and they are regarded provisionally as the Brachypodium pinnatum-community. They are especially rich in herbs and are distinguished from the other pasture communities by the absence of transitional types. Grasslands belonging to the association Nardetum montanum Sillinger 1933 are present in 2 relevs. They occur only in the highest localities of the region. The economic importance of the different types has been indicated on the basis of the fodder values of the individual communities.

4181324| Pollen spectra of three samples of dust taken from four medieval books are reported. The books, printed A.D. 1500-1530, were preserved in the Franciscan monastery of Kada (NW Bohemia) up to c. 30 years ago, and thereafter in Prague. Sample 1 contains rather few pollen grains, most of which are derived from cereals, probably from pastries or bread. Sample 2 is rich in pollen, containing abundant tree pollen, mainly Quercus and Fagus, indicating that the dust indeed comes from NW Bohemia rather than from Prague. Its overall pollen spectrum also corresponds well to published data from medieval forests and the cultural landscape of the region. The spectrum of sample 3 (two books) is rather rich in pollen, mainly of synanthropic plants. The remarkably high pollen numbers of cultivated plants (Sambucus nigra, Lathyrus type and Symphytum) are still unexplained. 
4181513|Eutrophication is often considered to play an important role in reed decline. We detected to use a chronological comparison of the two phenomena as a useful aid in the search for a possible causal relationship between them. Eutrophication is usually documented by changes in phosphorus and nitrogen content in water but there are no such data older than 10 years available for most of the lakes in which reed decline has been observed. The entire historical record of eutrophication has been recently reconstructed from micropaleontological analysis of indicatory diatom frustules, deposited in sediments in three lakes in south Germany. In these lakes, reed decline was well documented by archival aerial photographs. The comparison of reed decline history with the reconstructed changes in water quality confirmed the coincidence of reed decline and eutrophication. Consequently, eutrophication cannot be excluded as a potential cause of reed decline in any lake in this study.
4179491| Die bisherigen Erkenntnisse ber die Variabilitt der Schotenlnge bei den untersuchten Taxa des Komplexes Arabis hirsuta (L.) Scop. (Novotn 1965) werden unter Bercksichtigung mancher Umweltfaktoren erweitert. Als Material dienten Pflanzen aus den Kultivierungsversuchen, in welchen der verschiedene Auspflanzungsabstand als massgebender Faktor wirkt. Die Methodik wurde dem Ziel, die taxonomische Bedeutung der Schotenlnge zu erfassen, angepasst. Durch die Wahl des geeigneten Materials und die Anpassung der Methodik wurde erreicht, dass der Unterschied der usseren und inneren Faktoren deutlich hervortritt. Wenn auch die Kultivierungsbedingungen die reale Merkmalsvariabilitt abgendert haben, blieben die relativen Verhltnisse und Beziehungen zwischen den Taxa gleich. Die Beziehungen zwischen den Taxa sind unterschiedlich. Die Ausntzung dieser Unterschiede beruht in der Trennung der Taxa Arabis sessilifolia und A. sagittata. Der taxonomische Wert der Schotenlnge hat seine Begrndung in der genetischen Differenzierung der untersuchten Taxa des Komplexes. Die Durchprfung des Charakters und des Umfanges der Variabilitt zeigt die verschiedene Empfindlichkeit der einzelnen Taxa auf. /// In the present paper the author has attempted to demonstrate the taxonomic value of the pod length. The methods were so arranged that the different characters of the individual taxa investigated under certain cultivation conditions could be ascertained. The variability is clearer if a larger number of plants and therefore a smaller number of pod lengths from each plant are taken into consideration. Since there were significant differences between the results of five and of three measurements respectively, objections could be raised if the number of measurements was reduced to three. The variability in individual experimental variants was investigated by means of variation polygons which were mutually compared. Graphical representation of the variability of characters makes it possible to evaluate the importance of a character for distinguishing samples on the basis of relative ratios. In general, a denser stand of plants diminished the pod length; it appeared in the graphical representation as a shift of the polygons to the left. During two vegetation periods the external conditions did not substantially alter the relative ratios of Arabis planisiliqua. Parallel with the graphical representation biometrical evaluation was carried out. For the solution of subsidiary problems - not feasible by graphical representation - the t-test and F-test were applied. These tests contributed to knowledge of the character and extent of variability of the pod lengths so that the real differences were ascertained correctly. The taxonomical value of the pod length was proved in the genetic differentiation of the investigated taxa of the Arabis hirsuta (L.) Scop. complex. The shortest pods are in the species A. sessilifolia, the longest in A. sagittata; A. planisiliqua occupies an intermediary position. In pod length and its variability A. planisiliqua and A. sagittata are much more similar than are both taxa to A. sessilifolia. In spite of the fact that this character is strongly influenced by environmental factors, under certain conditions it may be used for taxonomical purposes. It has been found that the investigated taxa are not equally sensitive to the distance of individual plants. This influence diminishes from A. planisiliqua through A. sessilifolia to A. sagittata. - The final result of the investigation of the significance of a character is to ascertain the taxonomical value of the pod length. The best use of this character is in distinguishing the taxa A. sessilifolia and A. sagittata. The supposition that pod length represents a valuable character for the analysis of populations is well founded. The usefulness of this character is especially apparent in the frequent populations in which both A. sessilifolia and A. sagittata occur. The significance of the difference in the pod length of these two taxa appears only if a comparison of the other investigated characters is made. 
4181399|The original definition of the guild is reiterated and the concept discussed and placed in the context of related concepts such as resources and competition. From this conceptual framework the current use of guilds in studies of plant community ecology is evaluated. We discuss the criteria with which species are assigned to guilds, the association of guilds with specific communities, the resource classes on which guilds are based, and the competitive relationships between species of a guild. We conclude that the guild is presently applied in a much more loose way as compared to its original definition. In particular, the a priori assignment of species to guilds on the basis of the use of well-defined resource classes is often relaxed. This obscures the insight that the guild structure may provide in the role of resource partitioning and competition in structuring the community. A more strict use of the concept is advocated.

4180243|A simple simulation model of the secondary shrub succession has been elaborated on the grounds of primary field data from abandoned fields of different ages in the area of Bohemian Karst. The model describes vegetational dynamics using adapted Volterra-Lotka equations for competing species. Carrying capacities and growth rates are expressed as a function of the depth of the soil.
4181396|The exchange of ideas and information between vegetation ecology and pollination ecology is relatively restricted, yet both fields have devised methods to detect the structure of species assemblages and communities. To promote the exchange of ideas between fields I compare approaches, concepts, and problems faced by researchers working in each area. Both vegetative and reproductive interactions may generate assemblage structure through ecological sorting or through character displacement. Vegetative interactions may lead to assemblage organization more often by ecological sorting and reproductive interactions more often by character displacement. Vegetative interactions generally operate over shorter temporal and smaller spatial scales than reproductive interactions and may be affected more strongly by temporal and spatial heterogeneity in abiotic and biotic environments. These differences affect how the concept of ecological niche should be applied to plants. The Hutchinsonian concept of niche needs to be significantly modified before it can be usefully applied to plants. Null models are a valuable tool for investigating both vegetative and reproductive structuring of plant assemblages; however, the procedures followed in the application of null models need further refinement. The appropriate formulation of the null model may require information that is unavailable, hence multiple models may have to be employed to "bracket" conclusions. The literature on pollination community ecology demonstrates that difficult decisions must be made about the likely processes that have generated the structure being tested, the relevant definition of sympatry, how guild membership should be defined and employed, and what constraints should be incorporated into the null model to impose realism. Differences in these decisions will affect the outcome of the analysis. While top-down studies of pattern have numerous advantages, they usually cannot identify the process(es) that have generated the patterns. Bottom-up, experimental studies can be useful for identifying the processes, but they can rarely be used to assess the structure of an entire natural assemblage. The optimal approach to studying assemblage structure is to detect patterns with top-down analysis and use experiments to identify the processes that generate and maintain the patterns.
4181102|Seventeen natural Bulgarian populations of the species of the genus Carex sect. Digitatae were studied morphologically and karyologically. Stepwise discriminant analysis was used as a multivariate test for the separation of groups of populations from different taxa and to find a subset of characters contributing most for this separation. The following taxa were found in Bulgaria: C. humilis Leysser var. humilis; C. humilis var. longifolia Stoeva et Popova, var. n.; C. digitata L.; C. ornithopoda Willd. subsp. bulgarica (Vel.) Stoeva et Popova, comb. n. Aneuploid series of some chromosome numbers were found in C. digitata - 2n=48, 50, 52, 54, 56 and in C. ornithopoda subsp. bulgarica - 2n=52, 53, 54, 56. C. humilis has 2n=36 and a much more heterogeneous karyotype than that of the above taxa. The values of the Euclidean distance between the populations vary within similar limits in both species C. humilis and C. digitata; this is not in accordance with the karyological results. The within and between population morphological variations were compared in each species. The first dominates in overall variation, which is probably connected with the very large populations and their mosaic space structure.

4180171| In den Gebirgen Povask Inovec und Mal Karpaty konnten wir das Vorkommen von Artenkombinationen und charakteristischen Standorten der Pionierschuttgesellschaften aus der Klasse Thlaspietea rotundifolii Br.-Bl. et al. 1948 feststellen Zu ihnen gehrt das Galeopsietum angustifoliae (Libbert 1938) Bkker 1942 und die Epilobium dodonaei-Seseli osseum-Gesellschaft aus dem Verband Stipion calamagrostis. In der Arbeit wurde erhhte Aufmerksamkeit der synmorphologischen und synkologischen Charakteristik und syntaxonomischen Einordnung gewidment. /// Relatively widely distributed plant communities of alluvial gravel riverbanks as well as screes in high elevations have been quite well documented so far on the territory of Slovakia. On the contrary there are almost no data on these communities from colline to submontane belts. During vegetation research in the Povask Inovec Mts. and the Mal Karpaty Mts. (Western Slovakia) the authors located pioneer scree plant communities of the class Thlaspietea rotundifolii, namely the association Galeopsietum angustifoliae and Epilobium dodonaei-Seseli osseum-community. Galeopsietum angustifoliae forms unistrate sparse small-areal phytocoenoses dominated by Galeopsis angustifolia and/or Chaenarrhinum minus. Therophytes prevail in phytocoenose structure. Floristical variability and the low homotoneity (0,239 sensu eka 1966) as well al low mean coverage value 27,1% can be considered important synmorphological characteristics of Galeopsietum angustifoliae. The phytocoenoses of this community are growing at the basal parts of furrows on dolomite rocks, in deluvial screes, at the bottoms, slopes and various gravel deponia in quarries. The substratum can be characterized as raw protosoils with a low content of clay and loam and a high content of skeleton. Owing to precipitation the fine particles are flushed to the lower situated soil layers. The distinguished layer formed in this way is capable of holding these elements back. By enriching soil by nitrogen compounds and humus as well, suitable conditions for the ecession of nitrophilous plants are formed. These species are regarded as differential species of the subassociation Galeopsietum angustifoliae polygonetosum avicularis. In the dolomite quarries on the southern slopes of the Mal Karpaty Mts. (near Loonec and Doln Lopaov) the Epilobium dodonaei-Seseli osseum-community occurs. It requiers deeper and loose soils as well as higher amounts of fine soil ingredients.

Neuh. 1964 is bound only to soils of calcareous substrata. The variant with Actaea spicata represents a moister type of this subassociation; it occurs on steep, shady and fairly moist foots of slopes. The typical variant can be seen as an optimum stage of the Galio-Carpinetum primuletosum veris. The variant with Cornus mas, on the contrary, occurs in warmer and drier regions. The Galio-Carpinetum luzuletosum Oberd. 1957 is characterised by relatively poor soils (Parabraunerde type), often with traces of gleization. The Galio rotundifolii-Quercetum occurs on heavy soils, affected by suspended ground water, in flat areas as well as on mild slopes. The distribution of this association can be seen from Fig. 1. 3. This form was classified under the Potentillo-Quercetum on the basis of mathematical comparison. The Potentillo-Quercetum appears on heavy, temporarily very dry and cemented soils in flat areas, dry southern slopes or mild depressions. 4179852| Gegenstand dieses Beitrages ist die syntaxonomisch-synkologische Charakteristik des Alnetum incanae Ldi 1921 in den Tschechischen Lndern. In the area studied, this association represents a montane alluvial forest whose distribution centre lies at altitudes between 650 m and 900 m (Fig. 1). In the Czech countries two subassociations can be distinguished: the hygrophilous Alnetum incanae calthetosum Knapp ex Neuhuslov-Novotn and the typical subassociation Alnetum incanae typicum Oberd. 1949. 4180589|Pinguicula rotundiflora (Lentibulariaceae), a new species from southern Mexico related to P. parvifolia Robinson is described and illustrated.
4179820| Die Ursachen bestimmter Schwierigkeiten bei der Klassifizierung von Apophyten-Gesellschaften nach der Zrich-Montpellier-Schule liegen in der rumlichen und zeitlichen Vernderlichkeit der Verbreitung und Vergesellschaftung einzelner Apophyten. Das Bemhen die Apophyten-Gesellschaften in der "Assoziationsrangstufe" zu typisieren, stsst auf methodische Widersprche der Schule. Die Apophyten sind als "Assoziations-Kennarten" kaum anwendbar. Die Begriffe "Apophyt" und "Assoziations-Kennart" schliessen sich schon nach ihrem Inhalt gegenseitig aus. Die Apophyten-Gesellschaften kann man nicht als Assoziationen im Sinne der Zrich-Montpellier-Schule betrachten. Deshalb werden einige andere methodische Lsungsmglichkeiten vorgeschlagen und kurz diskutiert. /// The paper analyses some reasons for difficulties with the syntaxonomic classification of communities of nitrophilous apophytic species. Particular attention is paid to difficulties with the incorporation of these communities into the phytocenological system. The considerable lack of unity in methodology when defining the syntaxonomic units at the association level is emphasised. These discrepancies result in different meaning ascribed to the "association" by different authors, and in substantial heterogeneity in the content of this concept. The method employed in defining any "association" must therefore always be stated in each paper. Inevitably these methodological discrepancies are reflected in the system of higher syntaxonomic units. Some authors regard certain apophytic and neophytic plant species as "character species" of certain associations. In the opinion of the author of this paper, the contents of the terms "apophyte" and "association-character species" exclude each other. Each apophyte shows at least two cenological optima: (1) in a natural cenosis (group of cenoses) from which it originates; (2) in an anthropogenous cenosis (group of cenoses) in which its occurrence is secondary. The distribution of a species often markedly differs in various types of anthropogenous communities and in different regions. It also varies in dependence on the history of human colonisation and the economic development of a territory. The present paper gives numerous examples of these phenomena. The last chapter of the paper mentions several new ways of classifying anthropogenous plant communities. The main problem is the large number of new and recently arising species combinations entered by many anthropophytes. Consequently, anthropogenous plant communities have to be studied and typified with respect to their continuous variation in both space and time. This requirement is fulfilled, for instance, by the new classification method after Kopeck and Hejn (1971, 1974a, 1974b) and Kopeck (1974). This method renders it possible to incorporate a great many anthropogenous communities into the phytocenological system. The synsystematic position of individual communities in the auxillary framework of higher syntaxonomic units is not rigidly fixed; it depends on spatial and temporal changes of their species composition.

4181398|Three issues are discussed relevant to the controversy over using null models and observational data on guild structure to test community-level predictions based on limiting similarity theory. First, I argue that most limiting similarity theory is not based on reasonable assumptions for plants and that the theory that is relevant does not generate any predictions about expected guild proportionality on a small spatial scale. Therefore, regardless of adequacy of the statistical methods, the predictions being tested by the body of literature using null models to test for niche limitation are unlikely to be relevant in most plant comunities. Second, assuming that the predictions are after all worth being tested, I argue that most tests using the guild approach do not provide adequate explanations of how the defined guilds could lead to greater competition within vs. between guilds. If this is not true for the particular guilds used, the predictions of guild proportionality or size constancy will not be valid. Third, I address the controversy over whether field experiments can provide more solid evidence than observational data about the role of competition in determining community structure by (1) suggesting methods of dealing with potential drawbacks of field experiments, and (2) suggesting alternative experimental approaches for directly addressing issues about community structure.

4180031|Vertical profiles of soil temperature and of the dry and wet bulb temperature of the air, relative humidity and wind velocity were measured within and above stands of Junco-Molinietum Preising 1951 (facies of Deschampsia caespitosa) and Caricetum gracilis Almquist 1929 on selected sunny days during the growing season. Evapotranspiration was computed by means of the heat-budget equation. The principal difference between the two communities has been found in the soil temperature. The stand of the Caricetum gracilis occupies a habitat with a cooler soil and with a higher ground water level than the stand of the Junco-Molinietum coeruleae, facies of Deschampsia caespitosa. The evapotranspiration per unit ground area was higher by some 20% in the Caricetum gracilis. The evapotranspiration per unit above-ground biomass was much the same in both communities.

4181462|Plants have three basic means of reproduction, by outcrossing, by selfing, and asexually. In most plant populations, at least two and often all three of these options are everpresent, so that individuals adopt mixed mating strategies at evolutionarily stable strategy (ESS) threshholds. Because mating systems are genetically controlled and affect genotype structure, they are liable to feedback. Productive habitats with a large standing crop are more likely to favour outcrossing, while unproductive habitats may favour asexuality or selfing, so that mating systems may change through seral development, even within the same species. Outcrossing tends to break up linkage disequilibria, but may also favour the creation of adaptive linkage groups. Mechanisms whereby male sexual selection, small population size and selfing can influence the genetic structure of populations are examined.
4181394|Variance deficit in richness is not reliable evidence for niche limitation. The main problem is the effect of limitation to individual plant module packing at small quadrat sizes, though environmental and historical patchiness can also confound the results unless patch models are used. More reliable approaches to community structure (assembly rules) are those that take into account the characters of the species - guild proportionality, texture convergence and limiting similarity tests. A informally Bayesian approach to community structure is advocated, accepting that some hypotheses have greater prior probability, such as module-packing limitations, but using all the evidence available to estimate the likelihood of all the ecological hypotheses. The problem of environmental patchiness can be largely overcome by patch models. These models also overcome the problem of spatial autocorrelation, because they are conservative in such situations. For guild proportionality analyses, the possibility of sampling bias is a particular problem; this should be borne in mind during sampling, and checks made for the possibility in analyses. In devising Monte Carlo tests for community structure, permutation tests (i.e. randomisation tests, using sampling without replacement) are theoretically and practically preferable to bootstrap tests (i.e. using sampling with replacement). The best test is the simplest one that incorporates the intended null model and uses the intended test statistic. Experiments have intuitive appeal, but field experiments have several severe drawbacks, including the inevitability of artefacts, and insoluble problems of when to record. In practice, field experiments have told us surprisingly little about community structure.

4179907| The growth rate of stand biomass, the seasonal development of vertical stand structure and accumulation of mineral nutrients were compared in two Phrogmites ecotypes; the stands occur in two different biotopes, littoral and limosal, situated in the littoral of the Opatovick fishpond in the South Bohemian fishpond basin. Microclimatological data including incoming global radiation were recorded in both biotopes during three growing seasons. The differences in morphological, chemical and production characteristics of the two reed ecotypes were in good relation with the edaphic, hydrochemical and microclimatological characteristics of their biotopes. These differences are reflected in a higher leaf area index, denser stand, higher production parameters and a higher efficiency in the conversion of solar energy in the limosal reed ecotype as compared with the littoral population. The differences in annual production and in energy conversion have not changed within seven growing seasons. 
4179569| The nomenclatural validity of the names published in Fabricius's work "Enumeration methodica plantarum horti medici helmstadiensis" has been revised, with special reference to those of monotypic genera. The arguments for recognizing these names as validly published are given, and also reasons for regarding them as unitary designations of species. After consideration of all the arguments the author is convinced that the names in question are not validly published generic names as they are to be regarded as uninomial designations of species. Special attention is given to the name Lamiastrum Heister ex Fabricius (1759), which has recently been adopted as the correct name for the genus generally known as Galeobdolon Adans. 1763, but is here regarded as not validly published. As the name Galeobdolon Adans. itself may not necessarily be regarded as legitimate on account of the inclusion of the type species of the name Galeopsis L. 1753 in the circumscription of the genus, the author here makes a proposal for the conservation of this name which has been so often used in botanical literature. The genus Galeobdolon is considered to be represented only by one aggregate with three species, the names of which are critically revised. For the diploid species occurring in the East Alps a new nemenclatural combination is proposed - Galeodolon flavidum (Hermann) Holub - and Hudson's concept of the type species of the name Galedobdolon has to be amended by a restriction. In an Appendix the results are given of a short revision of the so-called "generic" names in Fabricius's work, with suggestions for further detailed investigation. At the same time some amendments to the List of "Nomina generica conservanda" are proposed, and attention is drawn to the necessity for certain changes in the citations of some generic names commonly taken up from Fabricius's work. /// Die nomenklatorische Gltigkeit der im Werke,,Enumeratio methodica plantarum hortimedici helmstadiensis, ed. 1., (1759); ed. 2., (1763)" vom Fabricius verffentlichten Gattungsnamen, hauptschlich der Namen der monotypischen Gattungen, wurde einer grndlichen Revision unterzogen; es werden nicht nur solche Grnde vorgebracht, die die nomenklatorische Gltigkeit dieser Namen als Gattungsnamen besttigen knnen, sondern auch Grnde, die ihre nomenklatorische Ungltigkeit als Gattungsnamen verlsslich beweisen. 4181031|Up-to-date crop production concentrates on the maximisation of plant matter production, both by optimum utilization of solar energy by plants and by the application of additional energy. Therefore a natural strategy is being developed aimed at combining the physiological functions of the assimilation organs with their external shaping and strengthening their variety in space and area. As demonstrated by many deposition studies, this effect is contradictory to the factors conditioning the low deposition capacity of plant covers. A high level of particle, gas and solution deposition increases the danger of food chain contamination and has a negative impact on plant production. Data concentrated on transport values of pollutants and their long-term dynamics in stands could be used for the selection of ideal crop types; therefore every effort should be directed towards selection and breeding.

4181106|The paper deals with the edaphic conditions of vegetation development on oligotrophic, wet alluvium. Field texture is of essential importance in the development of the mud vegetation of dwarf-plants. Soil consisting of a high proportion of small primary particles is able to store appropriate quantities of water, and transfers water to the plants with difficulty. Thus, the species which have adapted to these conditions have a competitive advantage over concurrent ones. The clay-rich soil hinders the availability of nitrogen. Hence, nitrophilous vegetation does not develop here. Due to the high adsorption capacity of the soil it may contain a large amount of available phosporus and potassium. The low osmotic activity of the soil is favourable for the development of the mud vegetation of dwarf-plants with a high cover degree.

4179622| Chromosome counts of the following 15 taxa are given: Eupatorium cannabinum, Gypsophila fastigiata, Helianthemum grandiflorum subsp. obscurum, Helictotrichon desertorum subsp. basalticum, Impatiens parviflora, Inula hirta, Jurinea mollis, Kernera saxatilis, Lembotropis nigricans subsp. nigricans, Malva alcea subsp. excisa, Myosotis nemorosa, Otites pseudotites subsp. cuneifolia, Plantago atrata subsp. carpatica, P. atrata subsp. sudetica, Poa badensis. 4180501| Man made stands with Pinus nigra Arn. were studied on limestone bedrock. They were planted out on biotops of previous calciphilous beech or xerothermophilous oak forests. The analysis of present phytocenological composition and the changes in ecological conditions, especially of nitrogen content in the soil, conduce to their classification, following the conception of Hada and Sofron (1980), as a new euhemerobic forest community, association Clematidi vitalbae-culti-Pinetum nigrae. 
4181547|A syntaxonomic revision of vegetation of anthropogenic metalliferous habitats (mine spoils of lead, zinc and copper mining) in the Eastern Alps (Austria, Germany, Italy and Slovenia) was made. The communities studied belong to the Thlaspietea rotundifolii (Linaria alpina-Cerastium uniflorum comm., Papaveri kerneri-Thlaspietum kerneri, Violetum dubyanae, Thlaspietum cepaeifolii, Thlaspietum rotundifolii, Scrophulario juratensis-Erysimetum sylvestris, Minuartia gerardii-Silene glareosa comm., Epipactido atrorubentis-Silenetum glareosae and Sileno alpestris-Moehringietum muscosae) and to the Asplenietea trichomanis (Sileno rupestris-Asplenietum). There is neither floristic support nor syntaxonomic justification for the concepts of the Galio anisophylli-Minuartion vernae, the Violetalia calaminariae and the Violetea calaminariae in the Eastern Alps. These units should be included within the Thlaspion rotundifolii, Thlaspietalia rotundifolii and Thlaspietea rotundifolii, respectively.
4181488|A critical species of the European flora, Allium fuscum Waldst. & Kit., belonging to A. sect. Codonoprasum Rchb., is investigated. The species was previously confused with other taxa of the A. paniculatum group, but on the basis of herbarium and field investigations A. fuscum is a rare chasmophyte, distributed in Romania and Bulgaria. The description, chromosome number (2n=16), taxonomy, chorology and ecology are provided. The relationships of this species with some related taxa of the A. paniculatum group are also examined.

4179829| Beim Studium der Keimungskologie von Cerinthe minor L. wurde ein neuer Typ der Heteromerikarpie festgestellt. Im Schizokarpium dieser Art werden 2 Typen der Merikarpien gebildet. Der erste Typ entsteht aus dem ganzen Fruchtblatt, ist zweifcherig und zweisamig. Der zweite Typ einfcherig und einsamig, entsteht aus einer Hlfte des Fruchtblattes. Beide Typen sind morphologisch leicht zu unterscheiden. Vom Gesichtspunkt der Keimungskologie verhalten sich beide Typen gleichartig. 
4181008|The rate of individual development and biomass of two subpopulations of Potamogeton pectinatus were measured in the heated and cool zones of the Patnowskie Lake in central Poland. P. pectinatus from the heated zone terminated its vegetation six days earlier than individuals from the cool zone. The rate of plant development and individual plant size from both stands were compared during their whole seasonal life cycle. At the final stage of development, the individuals from the heated zone were smaller than those from the cool zone. The data obtained from the measurements were treated by statistical analysis using the MANOVATEST.
4179489|Carex bigelowii complex is a group of taxa distributed over the whole Arctic region and in the mountains of the temperate zone. The species was described from the White Mountains in the eastern part of USA. The plants from Central Europe, the British Isles and Fennoscandinavian mountains differ from the plants of the typelocality in a number of characters, especially in the character of the inflorescence. On the basis of these differences the European plants represent a new taxon which is described as Carex bigelowii Torr. ex Schweinitz subsp. nardeticola Holub, subsp. nova. Very closely related plants to the new taxon are known from Central Siberia and from the Arctic region.
4181301|"Vegetation Structure and Species Co-existence" was the topic of a symposium organized in 1992, in Tartu, Estonia. The symposium was dedicated to the memory of Professor Teodor Lippmaa (1892-1943), who made important contributions, especially to the concept of synusia in community ecology. Current views on relation between vegetation structure and species co-existence vary. This variation is partly due to the traditional opposite views of plant community structure (the individualistic and organismic concept); these views refer both to the strength and role of biotic interactions within a community, and to the community structure.
4180986|Two Chenopodium species (C. album L., C. suecicum J. Murr) were grown under field conditions with sugar beet to assess the weed-caused crop loss, and with spring wheat in a replacement series experiment. The weeds strongly reduced the growth of sugar beet. Dew's competition indexes for the regressions of sugar beet yield on weed density were 6.81 and 3.78 for C. suecicum and C. album respectively. On the other hand, the yield of spring wheat was not affected by the two Chenopodium species owing to early shading of the weeds by the faster growing crop stand.

Germany and distributed in the Atlantic and Sub-atlantic regions of Western and Central Europe. 4180197|It is suggested that communities of cultivated forests can be incorporated into the system of "natural" wood communities either as facies, variants or subassociations, if they differ below the association level; if they differ on the association level, a new association is suggested, with the prefix "culti-" before the planted dominant tree species. Most of our planted forest communities differ on the level of association or less; the communities of Robinia are the exception. The authors agree with Jurko (1963) in classifying them as individual associations, alliances, order and class.

4181140| Description and drawings of Cephaloziella longii Va, sp. nova, from Bhutan are presented. This species is characterized by filiform shoots, very small leaves which are narrower than the stem and dioecious inflorescences. 
4181173|Names of species and subspecies from Janchen's Catalogus were revised with regard to their validity; invalidly published names were compiled in a commented list of 120 names. About sixty of them were analyzed at length from nomenclatural and taxonomical viewpoints. The cause of the invalidity of these names were discussed; omission of citations of basionyms to proposals of new nomenclatural combinations is the main reason for the invalidity of Janchen's names. Taxonomic reclassifications and nomenclatural revisions resulted in 23 new nomenclatural combinations, five of these proposals representing direct validations of Janchen's invalidly published names. Some more general problems of nomenclature are discussed: indirect validation of invalidly published names; omission of infraspecific homonymy; the correctness and necessity to attach neglected authors' names to the names of plants based on those names distinctly taken over from such authors; problems of autonyms in the ICBN Code. The use of the category "convarietas" in cultivated plants (instead of subspecies) is emphasized. Names validated by Janchen himself in his paper of 1959 should be used with this publication place instead of their invalid publication in the Catalogus. Some propositions for future research by other authors are also added.

4179854| The authors present the results of basic stratigraphic investigation, pollen analyses and macroscopic analyses of plant remains concerning two buried peat profiles and their mineral covers in the Zbudovsk blata marshes near esk Budjovice (southern Bohemia, Czechoslovakia). Both profiles (JC-9-A and JC-9-B) are characterized by two phases of sedimentation - earlier organogenic (Dryas III, Pre-boreal, Boreal periods) and later minerogenic (Sub-atlantic period). A stratigraphic hiatus appears between these two phases. The palaeoecological investigation supports the existing information about the rare occurrence of Corylus in some areas of Czechoslovakia during the Boreal period, brings proofs of fir forests in the area of the esk Budjovice Basin in the early Sub-atlantic period, and yields new data on the palaeophytogeography of some aquatic, swamp and mire plants. The paper also attempts to reconstruct the succession of local peat-forming communities. A comparison of the development of vegetation in the esk Budjovice Basin and in the neighbouring Tebo Basin is appended.

4181352|Two naturally coexisting grassland species - Centaurea jacea (often predominating) and Fragaria vesca (subordinate) were grown together in a pot experiment of factorial design, where competition and arbuscular mycorrhiza (AM) inoculation were used as treatments. The effects of competition were one-sided, i.e. the mass of F. vesca decreased relatively more than that of C. jacea as a result of competition. The root and total mass of C. jacea increased with AM inoculation while F. vesca did not respond. The mass difference between C. jacea and F. vesca in a particular pot increased when plants were mycorrhizal, mostly due to the mass increase of C. jaceae. This can be explained by the differential response of these species to AM. We did not find any indirect indication of the interplant transfer of resources. The results of this experiment show the more unbalanced competition (larger differences in biomass) resulting from AM infection of plants.
4179678| In dieser Arbeit werden Ergebnisse phytoznologisch-kologischer Forschungen der nordund mittelmhrischen Carpinion-Gesellschaften zusammengefasst. Das westtschechoslowakische Galio-Carpinetum Oberd. 1957 (mit drei Subassoziationen), das (vor)karpatische Caricipilosae-Carpinetum R. et Z. Neuh. 1964 (mit fnf Subassoziationen) und das schwach boreokontinentale Tilio-Carpinetum Traczyk 1962 (mit vier Subassoziationen) werden hier behandelt. Die Beziehungen der einzelnen Gesellschaften zu Gelndefaktoren, Bodentypen, einigen physikalischen und chemischen Bodeneigenschaften sowie die Verbreitung der wichtigsten Carpinion-Assoziationen in Mhren und ihr mathematischer Vergleich werden ebenfalls bercksichtigt. /// This paper gives the results of phytocoenological-ecological research of the oak-hornbeam communities of Central and Northern Moravia (incl. Moravian Silesia). The region of Moravia is especially interesting in this respect, because the boundaries of the area of the four important associations of the alliance Carpinion, namely the West-Czechoslovakian Galio-Carpinetum Oberd. 1957, the (Sub)Carpathian Carici pilosae-Carpinetum R. et Z. Neuh., the slightly Boreocontinental Tilio-Carpinetum Traczyk 1962 and the Pannonian Primulae veris-Carpinetum R. et Z. Neuh. 1964 pass through Moravia. The potential distribution of these associations in Moravia is demonstrated in fig. 10. The phytosociological structure of the first three associations occurring in the studied area is to be seen in Tab. 1-3. The Tilio-Carpinetum Traczyk 1962 as a new association for Czechoslovakia is analysed in detail in this paper. New subassociations are described: Tilio-Carpinetum molinietosum arundinaceae (differential species: Betula pubescens, Carex brizoides, Frangula alnus, Lysimachia vulgaris, Molinia arundinacea, Pteridium aquilinum, Vaccinium myrtillus, or Melampyrum pratense), a community of acid, periodically moist soils, and Carici pilosae-Carpinetum primuletosum elatioris (differential species: Primula elatior, Ficaria verna, Galeobdolon vulgare, Paris quadrifolia, Astrantia major, Arum maculatum, Gagea lutea), a community of a transition character to Tilio-Carpinetum. The mathematical analysis shows a relatively high degree of floristic homogeneity of all associations (index about 50%), clear-cut floristic difference between Galio-Carpinetum and Tilio-Carpinetum, and relatively high degree of similarity between Galio-Carpinetum and Carici pilosae-Carpinetum, as well as between Carici pilosae-Carpinetum and Tilio-Carpinetum. The comparison of habitat factors confirmed coincidence between the described associations and/or subordinated units, and relevant soil types. All associations occur mostly on fresh to dry, rarely on moist soils, with favourable physical properties, the top-soil being loose or only moderately compact and relatively well aerated. The chemical soil properties vary considerably; they show only weak relation to the syntaxonomical units. On the average, the most favourable soil reaction and chemical properties of soils were found in Carici pilosae-Carpinetum, less favourable conditions in Galio-Carpinetum, and worst in Tilio-Carpinetum. The physical and chemical properties of the top-soil (humus horizons) are most important from the ecological point of view. The content of nutrients in the sub-soil horizons seems to be rather unimportant with regard to the floristic composition of the studied plant communities. A general description of the habitat of the studied communities is given on p. 252-254. 
4180641| Stratigraphic, pollen and macroscopic analyses of the Holocene limnic and peat sediments from the eabinec fish-pond (southern Bohemia, Czechoslovakia) are presented and evaluated. 4181081| The seedlings of twenty eight annual and perennial desert plants belonging to fifteen families were raised under controlled growth conditions and subjected to a range of tests. The water use efficiency, photosynthesis, extreme temperatures and drought tolerance were monitored. The results were discussed for their ecological significance as a basic information to applied research. Seedlings which were more tolerant to extreme high and low temperatures and drought were more capable of controlling water loss through better water use efficiency. At temperatures below 25 C, the annual plants had higher photosynthetic rate than perennials, whereas at higher temperatures, the perennials were advantaged.

Xanthium are briefly discussed. /// Im Artikel sind neue nomenklatorische Kombinationen vorgeschlagen, die vom Studium der Problematik einer natrlicheren Begrenzung von verschiedenen Gattungen hervorgegangen sind. In den meisten Fllen handelt es sich um Ergnzungen der frher angenommenen Gattungsgliederungen durch weitere Arten; so z. Dans la partie gnrale, l'auteur dcrit brivement la morphologie et l'anatomie de ces derniers et indique sommairement les caractristiques des principaux types de stations o ils se rencontrent dans la nature, ainsi que leur rpartition gographique. Le problme de la position systmatique du genre Thelopsis est trait de plus prs. Dans ce but est adopte une nouvelle classification des principaux types de Pyrnocarpes lichniss, base sur les caractres de la paroi des asques, de leur appareil apical, des paraphysoides, des priphyses et des spores. Cette nouvelle classification, que l'auteur prsente comme provisoire, s'loigne notablement,  beaucoup d'gards, des conceptions qu'on avait jusqu'ici de la systmatique de ce groupe. De la comparaison de ces points de vue diffrents on arrive en ce qui concerne le genre Thelopsis, aux conclusions suivantes: 1. Le genre Thelopsis Nyl., les espces "Microglaena" rosea Serv. et "Clathroporina" heterospora Zahlbr., ainsi que la famille des Porinaces (s. str.) telle qu'elle a t nouvellement dlimite dans ce travail, constituent, en raison de leurs asques unituniqus et de leurs vritables paraphyses, un groupe trs isol phylogntiquement du reste des Pyrnocarpes lichniss, ordinairement bituniqus. 2. C'est avec les espces "Microglaena" heterospora (et vraisemblablement aussi d'autres espces de Clathroporina) que le genre Thelopsis prsente le plus de parent; et peut-tre sera-t-il possible ultrieurement d'ajouter a ce genre, ces espces qui par contre n'ont aucune affinit avec les Microglaena et Clathroporina typiques. 3. En ce qui concerne la structure des fructifications, il existe une grande concordance entre toutes les espces de Thelopsis, "Microglaena" rosea et "Clathroporina" heterospora, d'une part, et les Discocarpes du genre Ramonia Stiz. (Thlotremataces s. ampl.), d'autre part. Du point de vue taxonomique le seul caractre qui spare ces deux groupes est le mode d'ouverture de leurs fructifications. Tandis que chez Thelopsis l'orifice reste constamment punctiforme, chez Ramonia celuici est d'abord punctiforme, puis son bord se dchire en formant des sortes de lobes qui se recourbent en mettant finalement  nu l'hymnium. Cette grande concordance, qui ne peut s'expliquer que par d'troites relations phylogntiques, autorise  classer le genre Thelopsis et les deux espces voisines dans la famille des Thlotrmataces s. ampl. Dans la partie spciale de ce travail l'auteur fournit la nomenclature et la description des 6 espces de Thelopsis connues jusqu'ici, ainsi que de brves indications sur les caractristiques des stations o ces espces ont t trouves, sur la rpartition gnrale de celles-ci et sur les chantillons tudis. En supplment les deux espces voisines "Microglaena" rosea et "Clathroporina" heterospora sont traites de la mme manire. Le texte est complt par 16 planches de dessins schmatiques  la plume relatifs  l'anatomie de toutes les espces de Thelopsis, des deux espces prcdentes et de quelques Pyrnocarpes lichniss typiques qui sont tudis en vue de rsoudre le problme de la position systmatique du genre Thelopsis. /// The present work gives the results of a taxonomic revision of the lichenized fungi belonging to the genus Thelopsis. In the general part the author briefly describes the morphology and anatomy of the species of the genus, outlines the characteristics of the principal types of habitats in which the plants are found, and gives information on their geographic distribution. The problem of the systematic position of the genus Thelopsis is discussed in detail. In this regard, a new classification of the principal types of the lichenized pyrenocarpic fungi is adopted, an arrangement based on the characteristics of the wall of the asci, the apical apparatus of the asci, the paraphyses, the periphyses, and the spores. This new classification, which is presented as provisional, is notably different in many respects from the concepts previously held regarding the systematics of this group. The following conclusions concerning Thelopsis can be made: 1. The genus Thelopsis Nyl., the species "Microglaena" rosea Serv. and "Clathroporina" heterospora Zahlbr. as well as the family Porinaceae (sens. str.) such as it has been newly delimited in this study, constitute all together, by virtue of their unitunicate asci and their true paraphyses, a group phylogenetically very isolated from the rest of the lichenized pyrenocarpic fungi, which are usually bitunicate. 2. The genus Thelopsis is most closely related to the species "Microglaena" rosea and "Clathroporina" heterospora (and probably to other species of Clathroporina) and it might be possible eventually to place them in Thelopsis since they have no affinity whatever with the typical species of Microglaena and Clathroporina. 3. In the structure of the fruits there is a great agreement among all the species of Thelopsis, "Microglaena" rosea, and "Clathroporina" heterospora on the one hand and the discocarpic fungi of the genus Ramonia Stiz. (Thelotremataceae sens. ampl.) on the other hand. From the point of view of taxonomy, the only character which separates the two groups is the manner by which the fruits open. While in Thelopsis the orifice consistently remains punctiform, in Ramonia it is punctiform at first and then its margin tears and forms lobe-like structures which recurve and finally expose the naked hymenium. This broad correlation of characters, which can be explained only as resulting from close phylogenetic relationships, justifies a classification of the genus Thelopsis and the two closely related species in the family Thelotremataceae sens. ampl. In the special part of this work the author gives the nomenclature and the description of the six known species of Thelopsis, brief notes on the characteristics of the habitats in which the species are found, the general ranges and the specimens studied. The two related species "Microglaena" rosea and "Clathroporina" heterospora are treated in the same way. Sixteen plates of schematic line drawings are provided relating to the anatomy of all the species of Thelopsis, of the two allied species, and of several typical lichenized pyrenocarpic fungi studied with the view of clarifying the systematic position of the genus Thelopsis. 
4180856|The seeds of 115 species in eighteen genera of the family Portulacaceae were examined with the scanning electron microscope. Longitudinal sections of seeds of representatives of all the genera were examined with the light microscope. Two broad groups based on shape of the seeds, ornamentation of the external surface of their testa, and the position of the embryo relative to the endosperm were recognised. The first group comprising three genera: Anacampseros L., Grahamia Gillies and Talinopsis A. Gray, have seeds which are pyriform with wings and trichomes, and an embryo that is more or less parallel to the endosperm, while the second of fifteen genera: Calandrinia H.B.K., Calyptridium Nuttall, Calyptrotheca Gilg, Ceraria Pearson et Stephens, Claytonia L., Lenzia Philippi, Lewisia Pursh, Lyallia Hooker fil., Montia L., Portulaca L., Portulacaria Jacquin, Silvaea Philippi, Talinella Baillon, Talinum Adanson, and Wangerinia Franz, are reniform without wings and with an embryo that is horse-shoe shaped around the endosperm.

4181554| Six transects were established on the edges of two deciduous forests near Krosno (Carpathian Foothills) to compare the species richness pattern of vascular plants, bryophytes and fungi. The transects had the shape of a cross with one arm 10 m along the forest edge and the other across the edge, 50 m into the forest interior and 12 m into the grassland. They consisted of 2  2 quadrats. The strongest edge effects were recorded for bryophyte, shrub and tree species richness, the weakest for herbaceous plant species richness. Overall vascular plant species richness and herbaceous species richness were higher in grassland than in the forest and peaked in grassland, 3 m from the forest edge. The shrub species richness was highest 1 m from the edge (in the forest) and the tree species richness 3 m from edge. Bryophyte species richness had roughly the same level across the grassland and within the first several meters of the forest, except for the 2 m zone on the edge itself where species richness was as low as in the forest interior. Fungi species richness was low in the grassland and on the forest edge and rose dramaticaly a few meters from the edge, remaining at the same level within the forest. The species composition across the forest-grassland border was analysed using detrended correspondence analysis. It revealed that in the case of bryophytes the increase in species richness did not correspond to a change in species composition, such as might have been caused by a general increase in bryophyte density.

4181016|Changes in chemical composition of autochthonous plant litter undergoing decomposition in litter mesh-bags exposed in a transect across four vegetational zones of a fishpond littoral were estimated during the spring, summer and winter season. The highest decomposition rate was found in all four zones in spring, the lowest one in winter. The decomposition was faster in the two aquatic than in the two terrestrial zones in the spring and the summer season. The litter was enriched with nitrogen and released potassium in all locelities and seasons. The uptake or release of other mineral constituents appeared to be specific for each zone and to depend on the season of the year.
4180587|Myriophyllum spicatum has been discovered in the Nile valley during the past decade. The rapid colonization seems to be influenced by changes in the Nile water regime after the building of the High Dam at Aswan.
4181423|Plants of the common reed (Phragmites australis (Cav.) Trin. ex Steud.) were treated with high doses of nitrogen in an experiment performed in a sand culture and lasting one vegetation period. Nitrogen treatment resulted in alterations of growth; the increased growth of rhizomes and stalks was connected with production of significantly shorter roots. The differences in root growth were connected with changes in the internal root structure. In rhizome-borne roots, treatment with high nitrogen reduced the formation of aerenchyma and lignified layers in subapical regions. No substantial differences were observed in starch occurrence in the roots under the two treatments.

4181278|The Park Grass Experiment at Rothamsted consists of a series of fertilizer treatments which have been applied to a species-rich hay meadow annually since 1856. Detailed botanical analyses of the plots between 1862 and 1992 were classified to one of the National Vegetation Classification (NVC) communities using the similarity measured by Czekanowski coefficient using computer program MATCH. Results indicated that "control" unfertilized plots were a relatively stable Cynosurus cristatus-Centaurea nigra dicotyledon-rich grassland. However mineral fertilized plots moved towards a species-rich Arrhenatherum elatius grassland MG1e after 50-80 years and remained there. Plots receiving nitrogen fertilizer moved first to MG1e then on to a Lolium perenne-Alopecurus pratensis grassland MG7D. Perhaps the most interesting plot was one which received a low rate of the soil acidifying ammonium sulphate fertilizer; the species composition changed towards a MG7D (Lolium perenne-Alopecurus pratensis) community between 1856 and 1903 but since then a liming treatment has been applied to part of the plot and the species composition on that part has recovered to a MG5 community resembling the control plots, taking 70-90 years to do so.

At the same time, attention was paid to syntaxonomic problems of the sand vegetation of continental origin in the European area. The suggestion for a new division of the sand vegetation of continental origin is based on the verified supposition that plant communities of the alliances Festucion vaginatae So 1929 and Koelerion glaucae Volk 1931 originate in the Pontic region of South-East Europe and that they are evolutionary derivates of the sand steppe vegetation shifted to the west. From this point of view, continental (subcontinental) sand dune plant communities are classified in the class Festucetea vaginatae So 1968 emend. Vicherek. Taking into account the areas of plants which assert themselves in the composition of plant communities of the sand vegetation, and the geographical distribution of the individual communities, the class is divided into two orders which give a true picture not only of the synchorology but also of their epiontological character. The order Festucetalia vaginatae So 1957 includes communities of the sand steppe of the Pontic and Pannonian regions. Its alliance Festucion beckeri Vicherek foed. nova is that of the Pontic area; the alliance Festucion vaginatae So 1929 is an endemic unit of the Pannonian area. 4181397| Variation in the number of species was studied in a subthermophilous grassland at a scale of 0.05  0.05 m during a 5-year period. The observed variance of species richness (VSR) was compared with a null model based on random distribution of species over a set of squares. It was found that distribution of species richness had more values than expected around the mean and less values at the "shoulders". Both tails fell within the predicted limits. Application of the procedures removing spatial dependence (random shifts, rotation/reflection method by Palmer & van der Maarel 1995) and environmental heterogeneity (patch model by Watkins & Wilson 1992) did not change the observed pattern. Using simulations in which the number of clumps and clumping intensity were manipulated it was found that the effect of the clumped spatial pattern on VSR results in a wide range of variances. Both variance excess and variance deficit were found more frequently than expected under the null model. To test the effect of the limitation to the number of individuals per square a null model was developed which included the observed number of plant shoots per square, the observed distribution of the number of shoots belonging to individual species per square and the observed spatial distribution of the shoots. The observed VSR was still lower than that produced by the null model. Therefore, it is concluded that at a scale of 0.05  0.05 m plant species combine in a non-random way in the studied grassland. It is suggested that the shape of left and right "shoulders" of the species richness distribution may be caused by different factors, such as positive and negative covariance between species, respectively. Their simultaneous impact can generate the observed pattern in species richness.

4181353|Changes in plant community structure after changes in some aspect of the environment such as nutrients or grazing is often ascribed to changes in competitive relationships among the plants. However, very rarely is competition measured directly in such experiments. To distinguish between the direct effects of environmental treatments and changes in competitive relationships, it is necessary to quantify the influence of competition on community structure and compare the magnitude and direction of this influence between environments. We describe an experimental approach to accomplish this that is based on the classic yield-density experiment of agronomy. The approach is called the community-density experiment and requires experimental establishment of a gradient in total initial community density such that absolute densities of each species increase but initial relative abundances of each species stay constant along the gradient. We define various indices of the magnitude of community-level consequences of increasing density that can be compared among environments such as different fertilizer or grazing treatments. We also discuss various practical ways of achieving the experimental density gradient that are suitable for different kinds of communities.

The following facts were ascertained: (1) The chemical composition of the species with narrower phytocoenological amplitude (those of alliance and association) reflects, more or less conspicuously, the conditions prevailing on the site, even though different biochemical properties of plants of various families are manifested here to a certain degree - e.g. Peucedanum palustre. (4) In agreement with a higher concentration of nutrients in soils in the valley of the Opava river, the concentration of most elements in plants growing in that valley appears to be higher than that in those in the studied areas in southern Moravia and SW. Slovakia. On the other hand, in the regions of Hercynia (Tebosk pnev Basin, drsk vrchy Hills) poorer in minerals, a lower level of nutrients in plant material was found (Tab. 3). 
4180811| Phytosociological records were made in 80 stands lying in 50 small woodland islands in the Wierzbanwka valley. The types of communities were distinguished on the basis of numerical classification of records. These were mainly fragments of the Tilio-Carpinetum association. For all the stands and for two groups of stands connected with various soils and localized mainly in the eastern or western part of the valley the statistical relationships between ten independent variables were examined (area of record, area of woodland island, its shape, distance to the nearest large woodland, mean distance to the three nearest woodland islands and others) and 10 dependent variables (number of species of trees, shrubs, herbaceous plants, species characteristic of the classes Querco-Fagetea, Vaccinio-Piceetea, Molinio-Arrhenatheretea, Rudero-Secalietea and others). It was found that the floristic composition of the communities investigated was connected primarily with the isolation of the woodland islands. With increasing isolation the total number of species decreased, as did the number of herbaceous plants and that of herbaceous plants of the classes Querco-Fagetea and Vaccinio-Piceetea, while the number of species of the classes Molinio-Arrhenatheretea and Rudero-Secalietea increased. Conditions of the habitat such as the inclination of slopes, shading, and soil fertility were less important.

4180318|Hybrid forms arisen in the process of introgression are of low stability. Changes in climate lead to absorption of hybrids by the ancestor for which this change is most favourable. Though the forms created by hybrid introgression are able to exist for thousands or even millions of years, introgressive hybridization in the cases known to us, as well as in the genera Picea, Larix, Pinus, has not opened and is not opening any evolutionary prospects.

4179732| Es bestehen Unterschiede in der Bentzung des Terminus Dissemination bei verschiedenen Autoren. Die einen bentzen ihn im Sinne der Aussaat, die anderen als Synonym der Verbreitung. Die Verfasserin versucht die Beziehung zwischen der Verbreitung und der Dissemination klarzumachen, und hebt die Notwendigkeit der Bewahrung beider Termini hervor. Sie fhrt einen neuen Terminus ein: apeptosporische Dissemination (fr den Disseminationstyp derjenigen Arten, deren Diasporen zur Zeit der Milchreife wegfallen). /// In the botanical literature there are differences in the use of the term dissemination. The author explains these differences as found in the papers of various authors, and makes an attempt to clarify the relation between the terms spreading and dissemination; she emphasizes the necessity to preserve both terms. In a survey of the carpobiological system she tries to explain more exactly the complicated mutual relations of both terms. The terms under discussion are understood by the author as follows: Dissemination-a single, non-repeatable process in which the seeds either fall out of the fruits or are shot off, or in which the diaspores are taken off from the mother plant by man or animals (intentionally or accidentally). In the wider sense of the term, there may be taken into consideration the dissemination of spores or of some kinds of vegetative diaspores, e.g. bulbillae. In no case, however, should the term dissemination be used in the case of subterranean diaspores.-Spreading, on the other hand, is a single or repeatable process in which the seeds, fruits, spores, or all kinds of vegatative diaspores are either removed by means of various agents from the mother plant immediately after dissemination or are transported some time after dissemination from an other site; it means that spreading can take place-unlike dissemination-without any connection with the mother plant. Dissemination is sometimes so violent that it results in spreading over short distances. To the established terms "tachysporous, bradysporous, or semibradysporous dissemination" the author has added a new term, viz. "apeptosporous dissemination". This term means a temporal dissemination type of those species whose diaspores fall off at the stage of milk ripeness and ripen fully only on the ground (Ranunculus spp., Viola spp., Dentaria enneaphyllos, some species of the family Borraginaceae etc.). 
4180039|Ecology and germination behaviour of the seeds of two categories of Cucumis callosus Cogn. has been studied here. The seeds were found to be rigid in their requirement of light and temperature for germination. 4181307| On the Karula Upland, South Estonia, the forest moss layer was analysed using a transect of 726 contiguous 0.2  0.2 m plots. The sample plots were classified according to a multistage clustering procedure based on the sequential use of algorithms with different criteria. Several obtained clusters are rather similar in species composition, but abundance relationships among dominant species are distinctly different. For detailed analysis of mutual relations among societies a formal definition of adjacency is proposed, and two aspects of the cluster continuum - transitionality and distinctness - are estimated. It appears that almost all resulting societies are very distinct (P < 0.05), but at the same time can be continual in the sense of transitionality. Spatial changes in vegetation along transects are also discontinuous. The null hypothesis assuming the independency of neighbouring sample plots type was refuted with P = 0.01. The spatial extent of different synusiae is typically several times larger than it should be if there were no structure in moss vegetation. 
4180561|Three species of Euphorbia (E. granulata, E. prostrata and E. hirta) exhibited both morphological and physiological adaptations in dry environmental conditions. High bound water, thick cuticle, dense hair covering and low stomatal index are some of the survival adaptations they developed under water stress conditions of the Indian arid zone.
4180070|Zonation of grassland lying behind a coastal lagoon in Ghana is described, and related to seasonal fluctuations in moisture, chlorinity and aeration. The distribution of similar vegetation on the West African coast is discussed.
4180283|One new endemic savanna plant species from Cuba, Polygala omissa sp. nov., is described. It is known only from the locality of Yaguramas (Cienfuegos province).
4181120|A new species, Mesadenella meei, found in Minas Gerais, Brazil, is described and compared with the other two known species of this genus. The description is based on live plants in nature and culture, alcolol-fixed flowers, and the type specimen. The floral analysis method (Alves 1990) was used to differentiate the floral structures.

4180814| From the sediments of the former Komoansk jezero Lake near Most, pollen analysis of samples linked with archaeological finds has been performed. One reference profile has been pollenanalytically elaborated, followed by pollenanalytical dating of various isolated samples. The samples elaborated were linked with the following cultural periods: of stroked pottery, of funnel beakers, of domestic specimens of Baden pottery, of corded pottery, of the Untice culture, and of the Middle Ages. A reconstruction of the natural surroundings in various developmental epochs, especially that of the vegetation, has been performed in the locality, in its close vicinity and in more distant neighbourhoods (Komoansk jezero Lake, the Podkrunohorsk pnev Basin, the Krun hory Mountains, the esk stedoho Mountains). The results refer to the Atlantic, Subboreal and Subatlantic periods. The differentiation of the Subboreal in the area under study is still uncertain. /// Es wurden Proben aus dem Komoansk jezero-See, die in irgendwelcher Weise mit den archologischen Funden im Zusammenhang waren, palynologisch verarbeitet. Neustupn, CSc. (Archologisches Institut der Tschechoslowakischen Akademie der Wissenschaften, Prag). Die Ergebnisse der palynologisch-archologischen Zusammenarbeit knpften an die Absichten von Prof. K. Rudolph und Dr. H. Losert an, die sich um dasselbe schon in den dreissiger Jahren ebenfalls an den Proben aus dem Komoansk jezero-See bemht haben. Die palobotanischen Analysen hatten zum Ziel das relative Alter der analysierten Proben zu ermitteln und eine Synchronisierung mit dem archologischen Datieren durchzufhren. Zugleich wurde die Entwicklung des Sees und seiner Vegetation rekonstruiert. Es wurde auch eine Rekonstruktion wie der nahen Umgebung, d. h. des Krun hory-Vorlandbeckens, so der weiteren Umgebung, d. h. des Krun hory-Gebirges und des Gebirges esk stedoho vorgenommen. In der vorliegenden Arbeit wird ber das Problem der sich steigernden Widersprche zwischen der Chronologie von Firbas, deren sich die tschechoslowakischen Palynologen bedienen und den Schlussfolgerungen, die am Beispiel des Komoansk jezero-Sees Neustupn (1985) zieht, diskutiert. Palynologisch wurden diejenigen Proben ausgewertet, die eine Beziehung zu den archologischen Funden aus der Kultur der Stichbandkeramik, aus der Trichterbecherkultur, aus der bhmischen Badenerkultur, der Schnurkeramik, der Aunjetitzer Keramik und der mittelatlerlichen Keramik hatten. Die Resultate der Pollenanalysen von Proben P 93 und P 94 deuteten auf eine ungenaue Datierung eines problematischen Fundes hin, der nachher revidiert und der Zeitspanne der Aunjetitzer Keramikkultur zugeordnet wurde.
