4179743| Vesicular cavities in the lava fields of Northern Iceland communicate by small openings with the ground surface. Aeolian sediments, called the Icelandic loess, deposit over the bottom of these cavities, together with the reduced light intensity and equable microclimate, create specific biotopes occupied by sciophilous bryophytes and Cystopteris fragilis. A new association within the alliance Ctenidion Stefureac 1941 - Cystopteri-Distichietum capillacei Blakov ass. nova - is described in the present paper.

4181275|Fifteen successional seres from man-made habitats in central Europe were compared and the occurrence of clonal species assessed on the basis of cover data. The effects of soil moisture and nitrogen (expressed using Ellenberg indicator values) on the performance of clonal plants were also considered. Clonal species formed the dominant component of vegetation cover in the majority of the seres studied. In moist sites, their dominance was more pronounced and the peak in their relative cover occurred earlier in succession. The relative importance of species with guerilla type growth tended to increase with time in most seres and after 10 years these were mostly more important than those exhibiting phalanx type growth. The prevalence of guerilla species after 10 years was more obvious in moist seres. Clonal species were able to become dominant regardless of soil conditions, whereas the dominance of non-clonal species tended to be restricted to very wet and nutrient-poor sites. Clonal plant species appeared to maintain their dominance for a longer period than non-clonal plants.
4181316| The syntaxa of the near-natural sand steppes (class Festucetea vaginatae) and their substitutes due to trampling (Chenopodietea) were studied in 1991 during the Ukrainian-Czech expedition to the Birjuij Island Spit (Azov Sea, Ukraine). Within the alliance Festucion beckeri Vicherek 1972 (class Festucetea vaginatae. So 1968 emend. Vicherek 1972, order Festucetalia vaginatae So 1957) three associations and five communities without rank are described, covering the vegetation variability along gradients of sand stabilization/soil development and salinization/moisture. Further, two associations of the class Chenopodietea, due to deer influence, are described. Four associations (Centaureo odessanae-Stipetum capillatae, Poo bulbosae-Caricetum colchicae, Secali-Cynodontetum dactyli and Heliotropio dolosi-Brometum japonici) are described as new. 
4180833|Seven associations of segetal vegetation are distinguished for the vast arable lands of Central Yakutia. Low species richness and the prevalence of annual weeds are the main features of these communities. Only two dominant species Sphallerocarpus gracilis and Saussurea amara represent Asian types of areals. Other dominants Fallopia convolvulus, Elytrigia repens, Chenopodium album, Brassica campestris, Lappula squarrosa, Scutellaria galericulata, Thlaspi arvense, Avena fatua and Crepis tectorum are typically cosmopolitan. The phytosociological system of the segetal communities is described.
4180886|The main features of autogenic bog development are discussed. Using extensive literature the changes in vegetation, surface topography, soil environment and hydrology are characterized. Oligotrophy and low pH seem to be the most important factors directing bog succession. The decrease in decomposition rates correlates with increase of the content of dissolved oxygen in the soil water. Due to substantial changes in local environment bog succession should be considered first of all as an ecosystem process. In comparison with mineral land communities bog succession is characterized by more deterministic development. Both successional convergence and divergence are observed. In every case the concrete character of bog dynamics depends on the spatial and temporal scales of investigation.

4181246|Higher syntaxa of the class Asteretea tripolium are reviewed. This class covers plant communities of the Euro-Asian continent on low- and medium-salinized soils with medium moisture conditions where perennial herbaceous plants (hemicryptophytes) of non-succulent character prevail. On the territory of the former USSR and Mongolia, the class Asteretea tripolium is represented by the following orders: Glauco-Puccinellietalia Beeftink et Westhoff in Beeftink 1962, Cirsietalia esculenti Mirkin et V. Golub ex V. Golub ord. novus, Scorzonero-Juncetalia gerardii Vicherek 1973, Halerpestetalia Mirkin et al. ex V. Golub ord. novus, Artemisio santonicae-Limonietalia gmelinii V. Golub et V. Solomakha 1988, Suaedetalia corniculatae V. Golub ord. novus. Superspecies and aggregations of species are used for the diagnosis of higher syntaxa.

4179479| Das in der sdtoskanischen Maremma klimatogene Quercetum ilicis wird in regelmssigen Abstnden von etwa 12 Jahren kahlgeschlagen, wodurch tiefgreifende nderungen in der Vegetation entstehen. Es wird in den ersten zwei Jahren ein Massenauftreten von Therophyten beobachtet und bald darauf eine allmhliche Wiederentwicklung des Waldes, die durch Stockausschlge der krftigeren Holzarten zustande kommt. Die hufig auftretenden Brnde bedingen hingegen das Entstehen des Ericeto-Lavanduletum als degradierte Dauergesellschaft. Die vorliegende Arbeit stellt einen Versuch dar, die wichtigsten Momente dieser Sukzession zu beschreiben, u. zw. mit floristischen Angaben und mit der Bearbeitung von Lebensformen, kologischen Synusien, Schichtung, Verbreitungstypen und Polyploidie. /// The Quercetum ilicis galloprovinciale is largely distributed in Southern Toscana and only here and there substituted by the Ericeto-Levanduletum stoechidis or still more rarely by deciduous forests; cultures and permanent meadows do not exist at all. The Quercetum ilicis galloprovinciale (Tab. 1) is here in a special subassociation (arbutetosum) that occurs on moderately acid soils and moist habitats; the subass. pistacietosum largely diffused in the western Mediterranean, has been found only outside the studied zone in the immediate proximity of the coast. The Quercetum ilicis is very seldom found nowadays as a real forest of lofty trees, as it is cut down about every 12 years; the substituting vegetation (Tab. 2) does not form a distinct association. The Ericeto-Lavanduletum (Tab. 3) develops on slopes on which after repeated fires vegetation and soil have been largely impoverished. It constitutes an acidophilous permanent association that consists chiefly of bushes and is represented in the zone by a special chorological subassociation. The substituting vegetation has been studied in its succession and the most important results seem to be the following: 1. The floristic composition shows great fluctuations especially within the first 3 years following the cut; afterwards large amounts of weeds strange to the forest often appear but the species of the Quercetum ilicis remain and become dominant after five to seven years. 2. The number of species consequently augments within the first years from 25 to 60. 3. The most diffused woody plant after the cut is Arbutus unedo and only some years later Quercus ilex becomes completely dominant. 4. The annuals augment very much within the first years (up to 50%), but disappear afterwards gradually. 5. The species that appear after the cutting of the trees possess seeds with very efficient means of dispersal, but in some cases it must be supposed that the seeds had already been present in the soil before the destruction of the forest. 6. During the renewal of the forest the percentage of polyploids augments remarkably. 
4180518| The present study describes communities of flooded sites (Agropyro-Rumicion) on the shores of Rozko reservoir in E. Bohemia. Sources of variation and phases of differentiation of these communities are described. The differentiation of these communities is predominantly determined by the original communities, by gradients of flood-water depth and of soil water content, by the pool of propagules available, and by increasing competition during the ecocycle. The structure of communities was studied by various multivariate methods (cluster analysis, PCA, DCA). Some comments on the methods used are also given. The necessity of studies of community dynamics was stressed as being very important for correct classification. 
4179776|The authors give measurements of osmotic values in 35 Cuban plant species, using the cryoscopic method. Osmotic values of plants correspond relatively well with environmental conditions, but in different species of the same habitat they may be different. The lowest values were found in Cactaceae (-1.6 to -6.2 atm.) and in epiphytic Bromeliaceae (-4.6 to -4.7 atm.), the highest in halophytes: -21 to -56 atm.

4181470|The development of the taxonomy of the European bramble flora is discussed. Previous taxonomic concepts were mainly (1) description of each different bramble bush as a species of its own, (2) treatment of bramble taxa with hybrid formulas, (3) arranging of bramble taxa as infraspecific taxa within an artificial system, (4) creation of special taxonomic units like "agamospecies". In modern taxonomy only well stabilized apomicts with a regional or wider distribution are taken into consideration and treated as species. Merely locally distributed brambles or the countless individual biotypes (spontaneous hybrids and their derivatives) are no longer a subject of special taxonomic treatment. The research into bramble flora has made considerable progress during the last 25 years, and the species of large parts of Europe are now well known including their distribution which is often illustrated by detailed maps.
4181512|Seed bank species-composition and seed-density were determined in a successional calcareous (alvar) grassland in western Estonia. Three similar study areas were chosen to compare two different successional stages: open alvar grassland and overgrown areas with young pine forest 30 to 40 years old. In both successional stages, the centre and the edge of a relatively uniform stand were examined. Fifteen soil samples (7 cm in diameter, 5 cm deep) were taken from each of twelve sampling sites. The seedling emergence method was used to estimate seeds in the soil samples. A total of 69 species were detected in the seed bank, of which 18 did not occur in the vegetation. Eighty-nine taxa were recorded in the vegetation and of these 38 were not detected in the seed bank. Fifty-one species occurred both in the seed bank and in the vegetation. The three most abundant taxa in the seed bank were Carex tomentosa, Linum catharticum and Plantago media, which together made up 49% of the seedlings recorded. Differences in the species compositions of seed bank samples from grassland and forest sites were negligible, although the species richness per area of the above-ground vegetation was significantly higher in the open grassland. The only species tending to be lost from forest site vegetation but still occurring in the forest soil seed bank were Arenaria serpylifolia, Cerastium fontanum and Linum catharticum. About half of all the emerged species from all samples belonged to the transient or short-term persistent seed bank. In the grassland sites there were more species which belonged to the transient seed bank than in the forest sites, where the seed bank contained more short-term persistent type seeds. The seed density was significantly higher in forest sites and lower in grassland sites, which may be explained by the better germination conditions in well-illuminated communities. On the basis of the current study it might be assumed that the soil seed banks of overgrown alvar grasslands which include young pine forests can play a certain role in grassland restoration management.

Vzda gemeinsam; von diesen unterscheidet sie sich u. a. durch den fadenfrmigen Thallus mit Trentepohlia-Algen. Ihre fdigen Sporen gehren zu den lngsten, die bisher bei den Flechten beobachtet wurden. /// The new genus and species, Conotremopsis weberiana gen. n. et sp. n., described from Tasmania, is distinguished by the following combination of characters: white, filamentous, woolly thallus with Trentepohlia as phycobiont, elongated keeve-like apothecia at first closed, later opening apically, unbranched paraphyses and cylindrical asci containing unusual long filamentous spores with transverse septa. The structure of the apothecium suggests close affinity to Conotrema Tuck. and Ramonia Stiz. em. Vzda. The genus is systematically intermediate between these two genera.

4179533| Der Autor hat im Jahre 1966 den ursprnglichen Fundort von Rosa sancti-Andreae Degen et Trautmann beim Stdtchen Szentendre in Ungarn besucht, wo der Strauch, nach dem die neue Art im Jahre 1924 beschrieben wurde, noch immer wchst. Er studierte auch umfangreiches Herbariummaterial aus dem Umkreise der Verwandtschaft der Art und auf Grund dieser Studien gelangte er zur Ansicht, dass Rosa sancti-Andreae Deg. et Trautm. mit der frher beschriebenen Art Rosa pomifera Herrm. bereinstimmt und daher ihr Synonym ist. /// In 1924 Degen and Trautmann described (in Jvorka 1924) a new species Rosa sancti-Andreae, endemic in Hungary. In the opinion of the authors this species is allied to R. tomentosa Sm. but differs from it by having glands on the margins of petals. Comparative studies of test material showed this sign also often on R. mollis Sm. and especially on R. pomifera Herrm. on individuals from various localities in the whole area. As R. sancti-Andreae conforms to R. pomifera Herrm. in other morphological signs (with R. tomentosa Sm. it is not closely related, however, and not even similar), there is no doubt that Degen's and Trautmann's new taxon is in fact Rosa pomifera Herrm. and that the name Rosa sancti-Andreae Deg. et Trautm. ought to be classed with synonyms of this species. 
4181131| The method of pollen analysis was used to study a profile sample taken from the Jestebsk blato mire, the Doksy District (northern Bohemia). The aim of the palaeobotanical analyses was to perform a reconstruction of vegetation and environment for geobotanical and archaeological research purposes. Sediments dating back to the end of the Late Glacial and to both the Early and Middle Holocene were pollenanalytically studied. The results of the pollen analyses recorded the development of vegetation during the end of the Late Glacial, Preboreal, Boreal and Atlantic Periods. Parkline pine stands of the end of the Late Glacial developed to closed pine forests, during the Preboreal. Even during the Boreal, the dominant pine formed forest communities were typical of the area under study, though trees with greater demands on temperature and moisture conditions continued to penetrate the existing communities. During the Lower and the first half of the Upper Atlantic Period, spruce forests and alder woods formed the dominant forest communities in mire. Nevertheless, Pinus was still dominant on extreme sites (both from the edaphic and geomorphological points of view). An early occurrence of Alnus and Picea is another characteristic feature of the studied area. The conclusions drawn from pollenanalytical results were used for the reconstruction of the past environment of the Mesolithic and Neolithic Ages. /// Die Studie legt die Ergebnisse der Pollenanalyse aus dem Moor Jestebsk blato im Doksy-Gebiet dar. 4181519| Recent hybrid speciation events between the diploid Cardamine rivularis and the diploid C. amara leading to the triploid C. insueta were investigated with random amplified polymorphic DNA (RAPD). The hybrid nature of C. insueta was confirmed by the additivity of RAPD markers which discriminate the parent species. An unexpectedly high level of genetic variation within C. insueta argues for several hybridization events and/or backcrossing with C. rivularis. A low number of nonparental bands in C. insueta indicates the younger age of this taxon. In contrast to the situation in C. insueta, low variability was observed in the hexaploid C. schulzii, a derivative species of C. insueta. C. schulzii probably originated recently by a single autopolyploidization event. The higher number of non-parental bands in C. schulzii is explained by the changing genetic variability of the parental populations. Evidence for potential gene flow across the ploidy levels is also provided.

4180440|The alpine zones of Ladakh are floristically and geobotanically very interesting. In the past these were poorly known botanically because of the ruggedness and inaccessibility of the area. The varied climatic conditions and habitat types have a main role to play in establishing the vegetation of these zones. A total of 122 taxa were identified from collections made during the summer months (July, August and September) of the year 1976. These areas fall in an altitudinal range of 4000 to 5000 m. Fifteen taxa are reported as new records for this region. Six different habitat types were recognised on the basis of local distribution of these taxa, viz. 1. Rocky and gravelly sites; 2. Alkaline swamps; 3. Silty and clay sites; 4. Stream sites; 5. Meadow and shrub fields and 6. Cultivated field sites. A comprehensive inventory of the flowering plants of this region is given in the paper.
4181549| A revision was undertaken of the high-rank syntaxa of the vegetation occurring in rock fissures, ledges and screes of mainland Greece and Crete. All published phytosociological relevs available were collected and subjected to numerical classification and ordination. Four orders (Androsacetalia vandelii, Onosmetalia frutescentis, Potentilletalia speciosae and Petromaruletalia pinnatae) comprising 8 alliances (one of them new) were distinguished within the Asplenietea trichomanis (rock fissures, clefts, and ledges). The scree vegetation was classified partly within the Thlaspietea rotundifolii (Drypidetalia spinosae with 2 alliances) and partly within the Daphno-Festucetea (Saturejo-Scutellarietalia - a new order, with 2 alliances). Ordination revealed clear differences in floristic composition of the alliances distinguished. The studied chasmophytic vegetation of Greece contains a very high proportion of endemics which serve as diagnostic species of the syntaxa. Further, an analysis of chorological species spectra suggested that the chorological homogeneity of a syntaxon should be considered an important diagnostic feature at high-syntaxon levels. 
4179873|The seeds of Merremia aegyptia are indifferent to light conditions for germination, which becomes 100% in the first 24 hrs. 4181422| Seasonal dynamics of total nonstructural carbohydrates (TNC) and of carbohydrate species (starch, sucrose, glucose, fructose) were followed in rhizomes of Phragmites australis at two sites of the Tebo Biosphere Reserve (Czech Republic): Brann sand pit and Romberk fishpond-western shore, which were classified (according to plant species composition and phosphorus availability) as oligotrophic and hyper-eutrophic, respectively. Phragmites stands at these sites were expanding and retreating, respectively. Rhizomes were sampled within terrestrial parts of the reed stands (at a water depth of about 10 cm). The levels of total non-structural carbohydrates were determined mainly by levels of starch and sucrose, while glucose and fructose were present at comparatively low levels. The most conspicuous differences between the sites were associated with autumnal and March levels of carbohydrates. In March, i.e. at the beginning of vegetative development, TNC and starch levels were lower at the hyper-eutrophic, as compared with the oligotrophic, site. Starch and TNC levels fell from August to September at the hyper-eutrophic, but not at the oligotrophic, site. At the low water depth investigated, the differences between stands in carbohydrate levels do not seem to be large enough to account solely for their different vigour. It is suggested that the effect of water depth needs to be evaluated in more detail.

Die Bodenbedingungen dieser Assoziationen wurden charakterisiert, ihre syngenetische Bedeutung und Aufgabe bei der Bodenentwicklung definiert. Gleichzeitig wurde die Bodenentwicklungsreihe vom Protoranker ber braunen Ranker, Braunerde-Ranker und Ranker-Braunerde zur oligotrophen Braunerde beschrieben. Das Polytricho-Scleranthetum und das Cerastio-Agrostetum wurden in den neuen Verband Hyperico (perforato)-Scleranthion perennis, das Veronico-Poetum bulbosae in den Verband Veronicion eingereiht. Diese Verbnde wurden in die neugefasste Ordnung Trifolio (arvensi)-Festucetalia ovinae der Klasse Sedo-Scleranthetea eingereiht. /// On the acid crystallic siliceous rocks of the Bohemian Massive in the district of the acidophilous oak forest of the alliance Quercion robori-sessiliflorae, in the territory of the middle part of the Otava river in southwestern Bohemia, the following acidophilous xerophilous grassland communities were described: Polytricho (pilifero)-Scleranthetum perennis on soils of the braun ranker, Carastio (arvensi)-Agrostetum pusillae on soils of the braunerde-ranker and ranker-braunnerde, Veronico (vernae)-Poetum bulbosae on soils of these associations with more or less disturbed surface. These associations are bound to southern slopes at altitudes of about 380-530 m. above sea level. The Polytricho-Scleranthetum differs from the Cerastio-Agrostetum ecologically primarily in the depth of the soil profile (Polytricho-Sceleranthetum ca 10-15 cm., Cerastio-Agrostetum ca. 30-60 cm.). The chemical properties of the soils of both associations are very similar. The soils have a low exchange capacity, a low reserve of exchangeable calcium, magnesium and potassium, and are unsaturated. A higher content of humus and also a higher content of exchangeable calcium occurs in the uppermost layer of the soil profile only. The similarity of the chemical properties of the soil of both associations resulted in little difference in the qualitative floristic composition (especially of the herb layer) of the associations under consideration; they differ mainly in the quantity of each species and the consequent different synmorphology. All the associations described occur in territory which is not reached by the migration-stream of thermophilous species penetrating from central Bohemia up the stream along the Vltava and Otava rivers. Therefore widely distributed species that can be considered only as "xerophilous" predominate in the species lists of these associations; the more thermophilous species are mostly missing. The Polytricho-Scleranthetum and the Cerastio-Agrostetum are stages of the succession series starting from initial association of vascular plants - the Asplenietum septentrionalis occupying the crevices and ledges of siliceous rocks-and continuing through the Polytricho-Scleranthetum and Cerastio-Agrostetum to communities that occupy deep mature soil. This succession is conditioned by the parallel soil development and itself influences the soil development in turn. On crystallic siliceous rocks soil development starts with the protoranker of the Asplenietum septentrionalis and continues with the braun ranker of the Polytricho-Scleranthetum to the braunerde-ranker and further to the ranker-braunerde of the Cerastio-Agrostetum. This soil development would end in the oligotrophic (or mesotrophic) braunerde that represents the climax soil type in these altitudes. To this soil type acidophilous oak forest of the Quercion robori-sessiliflorae would correspond as the climax vegetation. The soil development is seen primarily in the deepening of the soil profile and its morphological differentiation. Changes in the chemical properties of soil are seen in increased exchangeable calcium especially in the upper part of the A-horizon. The succession series described can be considered as primary only in its first stages-Asplenietum septentrionalis and Polytricho-Scleranthetum. The Cerastio-Agrostetum is without doubt a secondary plant community protected against the invasion of woods by man's activity. The Veronico-Poetum can be considered even as a tertiary plant community replacing the Polytricho-Scleranthetum and the secondary Cerastio-Agrostetum on soils with  disturbed surface as the initial stage of a subseries. In deciding the position of the associations described in the phytocenological system the existing systems of different authors were discussed, including on the one hand plant communities of shallow soils in solid rocks and on the other hand plant communities of consolidated or even wind-blown sands. For each plant community unit the validity of its publication was verified and its correct name was established. For classification of the Polytricho-Sceranthetum and the Cerastio-Agrostetum a new alliance -the Hyperico (perforato)-Scleranthion perennis was proprosed. The Veronico-Poetum bulbosae was classified in the alliance Veronicion. Both these alliances were arranged in a new order-the Trifolio (arvensi)-Festucetalia ovinae of the class Sedo-Scleranthetea. A new classification within the Sedo-Scleranthetea was proposed.

Mit deren Hilfe konnten die Verfasser die relativ reichen epiphyllen Flechtensammlungen bestimmen, die grsstenteils vom jngeren Autor (K. K.) im tropischen Amerika selbst gesammelt, teilweise auch von mehreren Fachkollegen den Autoren zur Verfgung gestellt worden sind. 4179482| Im ersten Teil dieser Arbeit werden die Studienergebnisse ber die Verbreitung einzelner Arten der Gattung Bidens aus den Jahren 1962-1965 angefhrt. Im zweiten Teil werden die Wege sowie die Art und Weise veranschaulicht, wie sich die adventiven Arten der Gattung Bidens in Mitteleuropa verbreiteten. /// In the years 1962-1966 the author carried out research on the distribution of species of Bidens in Czechoslovakian streams and ponds. Bidens frondosus and Bidens radiatus were mapped throughout the country; Bidens cernuus only in Slovakia, because it has a very wide distribution in lowlands and in the submontane belt all over Bohemia and Moravia; Bidens tripartitus was not mapped at all for the same reason. The distribution of Bidens radiatus in Bohemia and Moravia is correlated with the phytogeographical districts. Most of the localities belong to the oligotrophic and mesotrophic substrata of Hercynicum. The centre of the area in the Hercynicum are the ponds of Tebo and Budjovice, as it is a species mainly of stagnant waters. Most of the Pannonicum localities are in Subpannonic districts; only one locality belongs to the Eupannonicum: in Mlnsk pond in southern Moravia. The species is lacking in Slovakia. Bidens frondosus probably started to spread in Czechoslovakia at the beginning of this century. In many districts of Bohemia it is now a common species. It penetrated to Slovakia later and it is still not widespread. Bidens cernuus is relatively common in lowlands and the submontane belt in Bohemia and Moravia; the optimum is to be found in springs. It is lacking in some lower parts of the Slovakien streams, probably due to hydrological conditions (high water in summer, the form of the river bed etc.). This problem should be followed up. Bidens connatus at present occurs in Czechoslovakia in one locality only-Karvin in Silesia (the river Stonvka); it has not been previously indicated in Czechoslovakia in other localities. Ephemeric occurrence of this species is known not only in secondary localities, but also in autochtonic occurrence. Simultaneously with the distribution some ecological problems of the species were studied. The reason why the adventitious species Bidens frondosus has proved stronger than Bidens tripartitus was established. Bidens frondosus germinates 7-10 days earlier than Bidens tripartitus. While Bidens tripartitus has only developed cotyledons, the second species has already 2 pairs of normal leaves. This advantage seems to be the main reason why Bidens frondosus prevailed over the indigenous species. When Bidens pilosus was cultivated in our experimental garden at Prhonice in the years 1963, 1964 and 1966, it has been found that germination takes place already in autumn; this leads to the extermination of young plants by frost, as they are not hardy. This species cannot be easily naturalized under the climatic conditions of Central Europe. All the species studied need places with relatively high amount of water in the soil at the germination time. Bidens radiatus and Bidens cernuus can only grow under terrestrical conditions for a short time. Bidens frondosus B. connatus and B. tripartitus grow on dry soil and fruit very well there in the later development phases. If we remember that Bidens frondosus was found by Krocker in 1777 on the river Odra (Oder) at Wrocaw, and that there existed several old canals connecting the river Odra and Labe (Elbe) with the river Wisa (Vistula), we can conclude that these three rivers need not be the isolated ways the adventitious species spread. The history of the spreading of adventitious species of the genus Bidens in Central Europe has three stages. In the first the species came to Europe, probably by synagestochory. In the second they spread mainly by nautohydrochory down streams and by epizoochory (endozoochory or synagestochory) up streams. In the third stage the species started to spread by means of epizoochory, endozoochory and synagestochory beyond the stream banks. 
4181464|Intraspecific variation of four agamospecies of Hieracium sect. Alpina was studied using RAPD and isozyme techniques. No variation in either multiprimer RAPD or multi-enzyme phenotypes was observed within H. holosericeum, suggesting that this widespread species consists of only a single genotype. A low level of within-population isozyme variation was seen in H. tenuifrons and H. calenduliflorum, the origin of which appears to be consistent with somatic mutation. Most isozyme and all RAPD variation in these two species was partitioned between populations. A strong correlation with geography suggests that its cause may be due to polytopic (=polyphyletic?) origin or perhaps to mutation and dispersal. The most variable species was H. alpinum, in which isozyme variation occurred mostly within populations rather than between them, suggesting occasional sexual events or that the parents of H. alpinum were heterozygous. RAPD variation in this species, in contrast, was partitioned between Scottish and Swiss populations, suggesting the existence of geographical races.

4179609| Caricetum gracilis Almquist 1929 ist eine Assoziation mit ausgedehnter eurosibirischer Verbreitung, es bewahrt sich jedoch in seinem ganzen Areal eine mehr oder weniger konstante znotische Zusammensetzung, die durch das Grundmerkmal - die Anwesenheit von Carex gracilis als Dominante (Kondominante) und difikator, bedingt ist. Als ausschlaggebender Faktor fr die Entstehung der Gesellschaft kommt der Wasserhaushalt mit charakteristischer Abwechslung der berschwemmungen und Austrocknungen zur Geltung. Die geographischen, klimatischen und bodenkologischen Unterschiede der Standorte ermglichen eine weitere Gliederung der Assoziation in Caricetum gracilis Subass. typicum mit grsstem Verbreitungsgebiet, die in drei Varianten zerfllt, weiter in Caricetum gracilis comaretosum, dessen Areal an nrdliche Teile Mittel- und Osteuropas gebunden ist und das in zwei Varianten zerfllt, und schliesslich in Caricetum gracilis naumburgietosum, das vor allem an das Herzynische Gebiet und den Nordrand der Karpaten gebunden ist. /// In the present paper a survey of existing knowledge of the association Caricetum gracilis Almquist 1929 (= Caricetum gracilis Graebner et Hueck 1931) is given and an evaluation based upon the author's investigation of this association carried out. From studies of Caricetum gracilis throughout Europe it is evident that the prevalent majority of stands of this association represent a substitute community of natural forest communities of the alliance Alnion glutinosae or Alno-Padion; it occurs most frequently and best developed in the inundated parts of broader valleys. Sporadically only, and over a small area, Caricetum gracilis represents the primary community of the filling-in series of stagnant or very sluggish waters. The decisive factor for the rise and perseverance of Caricetum gracilis is the rhythm of the water regime of the habitat, characterized by flood alteration (especially in the springtime) and by at least temporary or longer-term sinking of water under the soil surface during the second half of the vegetation season. If the water regime (and therefore also that of the air) is convenient, the rise of the association is further dependent upon the nutritive conditions of the soil (the enrichement of soil through turbid flood water plays an important role here). The soil type is mostly anmoor (mainly the subtype warp anmoor in the northern part of the distribution area also the subtype peat anmoor). The community only occurs on other soil types in limiting cases - in the initial stages in the filling-in series (fen) or after drainage (gley). The essential feature of the association is the function of Carex gracilis (only one characteristic species) not only as dominant or condominant, but also as the building-up species (edificator), by which the other characters of the cenosis are to a considerable degree determined. Furthermore, in the building-up the community it is mainly the species of superior units or of other parallel units of the class Phragmiti-Magnocaricetea which take part; frequently species of units belonging to the classes Molinio-Arrhenatheretea and Scheuchzerio-Caricetea fuscae and to the alliance Agropyro-Rumicion crispi also take part. The participation of mosses is variable and for the existence of association is not very significant. Monospecific stands of Carex gracilis alone (although this sedge may be very vital in them) are not a typical form of the community and usually represent only a temporary phase. Variable dynamics, regarding both the quantitative and often also the qualitative composition of the community are indeed characteristic of the association and result from its substantial dependence on the changeable conditions of the habitat. On the other hand, however, the community is very resistant against disturbing interferences (temporary changes of habitat); it bears unfavourable conditions for years (though in changed phases) without being destroyed. The association is distributed mainly in the temperate zone of Central and Eastern Europe (perhaps in Siberia, too). Its distribution maximum as well as the most varied differentiation are to be found in the northern part of Central Europe and probably also in the forest zone of Eastern Europe. In the more southern, i.e. more arid regions it is bound more strictly to those parts of larger river valleys which are flooded for long periods. When the syntaxonomical position of this association and its sub-units was dealt with, only those characters were taken into consideration as classification criteria, which are most essential at the respective level. When defining the association on the basis of the building-up position of Carex gracilis, the author started from the assumption that the position of Carex gracilis as edificator is a constant character by which the variability of the cenosis is at the same time limited to a high degree. The differences in the participation of species belonging to various specific groups (by which mainly the deviations of the water and nutrition regime as well as of the climatic and geographic conditions are indicated) make it possible to distinguish several sub-units. The fundamental subassociation - obviously widespread all over the distribution area of the association - is subass. typicum Uhlig 1938 em. Blakov, without special differential species. This subassociation is mainly bound to mineral soils of inundated sites. Within the scope of the subassociation three variants have been distinguished by the author: var. typicum, which is characterized by the lowest number of species and occurs in the moistest sites; var. with Festuca pratensis, which is characterized by a group of differential species belonging to units of the class Molinio-Arrhenatheretea and is bound to more drying-up habitats; and var. with Gratiola officinalis, which represents a Pannonian-Illyrian geographical race and differs - besides the differential species which are all very little constant - also by a slightly shifted ratio of species belonging to individual cenotic groups. The subass. comaretosum Passarge 1955 possesses as differential species mainly the characteristic and differential species of the alliance Magnocaricion (= Caricion rostratae Bal-Tul. 1962). Conspicuous is also the higher total share of species belonging to the units of the class Scheuchzerio-Caricetea fuscae. The subassociation divides into var. comaretosum (= typicum), without any differential species, and into var. with Ranunculus repens, which to a certain degree bears resemblance to subass. typicum. A new subass. naumburgietosum has been described. The differential species group of which resembles that of subass. comaretosum, but in the floristic respect it differs quantitatively - by a different ratio of differential species as well as by a different ratio of participation of species belonging to individual cenotic groups. In denominating the units priority rules have been observed, however, some names used in the literature are synonyms, or the units designated by them have been included in units denominated before. At the end of this paper the economic evaluation of the stands of the Caricetum gracilis has been carried out and ways of most productive exploitation and amelioration have been suggested.

4180367|The following bioclimatological characteristics were measured on differently aged successional stages of abandoned fields: temperature on soil surface under snow layer, and depth of frozen soil in period of culminating frosts, daily course of temperature in top soil layer; maximum temperature in top soil layer during first half of June. 4181305| This study presents results of a three and a half year experiment in a calcareous grassland on the Baltic island of land, south-eastern Sweden. Environmental conditions, viz. nutrient regime, water availability, light conditions and grazing pressure were changed in a randomised experimental design with ten different combinations of these factors, including a control. Weather conditions during the study period fluctuated considerably. Only the combination of reduced light and increased soil nutrient availability decreased species richness significantly, presumably by inducing asymmetric competition for light by competitively strong species. Physical space also became less available for weaker competitors. In cases where only nutrients or only water were supplied in sufficient amounts, competitive exclusion was inhibited by either low nutrient or low water availability. Under conditions which combined high levels of nutrient and water supply with regular disturbance (i.e. simulated grazing) high species richness was maintained. Although there was a significant negative correlation between species richness and amount of above-ground biomass, the number of species was not significantly reduced in the treatment which combined fertilisation and irrigation. One reason for this may be that the heterogeneous light regime in this treatment still allowed species persistence and coexistence. 
4181271| We present a literature survey of studies using molecular markers to investigate genet diversity and structure in clonal plants. The data from 40 studies comprised 45 species of which only two were studied by DNA methods, the rest by isozyme markers. Less than one third of the studies provided information about the spatial distribution of individual genets within populations, and only 12.5% of the studies used mapping of all ramets within plots or part of the population in combination with identification of multilocus genotypes. We also present two case studies. In Glechoma hederacea morphological criteria were used to select clones. Multi-samples of ramets within these "clones" turned out to be variable using isozymes indicating that these "clones" in most cases consisted of several genets. One individual multilocus genotype covered tens of square metres. In Hylocomium splendens samples from 10  10 cm plots usually consisted of a mixture of multilocus genotypes, but occasionally the whole plot consisted of one genet.

Die Art kommt bei uns bisher nur als Epoekophyt vor. Sie wurde Dank ihrer biologischen Eingeschaften unter Quarantnunkruter eingereiht. Zum Vergleich werden auch kurze Angaben ber die Chorologie und kologie der S. volgense im Ausland beigeschlossen. Die Mehrheit der Lokalitten im Gebiet des sekundren Areals verdankt ihren Ursprung vor allem der Einschleppung der Diaporen mit eingefhrten sowjetischen Getreide. Ausser der UdSSR, wo die Art in Steppen im Sdosten des europischen Teiles einheimsich ist und wo sie in Europa auch ausser dem Gebiet ihres ursprnglichen Areals verbreitet ist, wurde sie vom J. 1880 in 12 europischen Lnderen verzeichnet. Ausser Europa ist sie bisher nur aus dem Fernen Osten der UdSSR bekannt. Nach Angaben aus den europischen Lndern verhlt sie sich expansiver in relativ kontinentaleren Lndern, wie z.B. in der Tschechoslowakei (51 Lokalitten), Polen (16 Lokalitten), Deutschland (eine grssere Anzahl Lokalitten), Finnland (22 Lokalitten), In westlicher Richtung ist sie in der Regel weniger vital mit einem beschrnkten Vorkommen nur auf einer oder einigen Lokalitten. In Zukunft kann man eine weitere Ausbreitung des sekundren Areals dieser relativ expansiven Art erwarten. 
4179448| Diese Studie behandelt die in der Phytogeographie allgemein bentzten Termini vom Gesichtspunkte ihrer Begrenzung und Vereinheitlichung. Jeder Terminus wird definiert, seine lateinische Bezeichnung, sowie auch Beispiele und in manchen Fllen auch Zeichnungen und Karten wurden beigefgt. In der Studie wird die Terminologie der horizontalen und vertikalen Einteilung der Erdoberflche, weiter die Terminologie verschiedener Typen von Arealen, Disjunktionen, Elementen, Endemiten, Relikten, Dealpinen, Vikarianten, synanthropischen Pflanzen, usw. angefhrt. /// The authors collected the terms of general phytogeography dispersed in the literature, evaluated them and in the present study they suggest proper terms to be used. Terms which were lacking have been created. Thus as far as the main results are concerned several items can be given: A new term "septentrional zone" is suggested for the temperate zone of the northern hemisphere; the term "boreal" which has been used up to now will be kept to designate a floristic region which is only a part of this zone. A double system for vertical division is used, i. e. a general one of which the vegetation-belt is the basic unit and a special one (elaborated here for the region of SSR) in which the basic unit is the vegetation-grade. The term "element" is used only in composite terms such as floristic element and region-element; instead of the term "genetic element" the term "ortant" and instead of the term "migrations-element" the term "migrant" are suggested; further the term "area-type" is suggested instead of the terms "geographic element", "component" and partially "geoelement". The authors differentiate strictly between the terms "area-type" and "floristic element"; in determining the area-type, attention must be paid to the whole distribution of the plants, the area-type can be determined for all taxa. The floristic element, however, shows a narrow relation of the distribution of the taxon to a certain natural floristic region and cannot be determined for all taxa. The floristic element can be further divided into the genuine floristi element, subelement, penetrant and conelement. The term "endemic" is suggested only for taxa of autochthonous origin, not for taxa with a limited distribution (area), where the term "microarealophyte" showed be used. With regard to this basic attribute of the endemic it is necessary to differentiate strictly between endemics and relics. For regions where relics have survived the following two terms are used: refugium and residuum, according to whether the region did or did not belong to the former area of the taxon examined. As to the type of relations of the taxa in the course of their migration regarding a certain region the following terms are suggested: restant, superstant, fugant, residuant, transient, demigrant, remigrant, reservant and immigrant. The term "praealpine" is not used by the authors of the present study in view of the different use of this term by former authors. The term "perialpine" is used instead of it for its original meaning. For the designation of taxa which extend from the lower regions of their original distribution to higher regions, the term "penalpine" has been suggested. For the classification of synanthropic plants a system is suggested, which endeavours to take into the consideration the basic types of relation of the distribution of the plants to human activity.

4180816|The present review gives an account of the applicability of mathematical modelling in ecological succession studies. The ability of particular model types to solve problems of both theory and management is discussed. The Markovian models are found to be useful for short term predictions, but of very limited value for theoretical considerations. Finally, the predictability of successional pathways is discussed. It is argued that the less we understand about processes in vegetation dynamics, the more we will see the course of succession as random and unpredictable.

4181541|The main objective of the present study was to attempt to assign different vegetation types in South Sweden to the Braun-Blanquet system of syntaxa. The alliance was chosen as the most appropriate phytosociological unit for this purpose. Coniferous forests represent the zonal vegetation in large parts of South Sweden: spruce forests on mesic to moist sites and pine forests on dry, often strongly oligotrophic sites can be assigned to the Piceion excelsae and Dicrano-Pinion respectively. In addition, various types of azonal vegetation (e.g., mires, springs, swamps and salt-marshes) subjected to some form of extreme environmental factor can be placed in alliances described from Central Europe. In contrast, some southern vegetation types in Sweden are difficult to assign, partly due to a lack of character species, as in the case of deciduous hardwood forests. In other cases, species of southern syntaxa are still frequent, for example in dry basiphilous grasslands and sun-exposed forest edges, but the syntaxonomical difficulties arise from an intermixture of diagnostic species of complementary alliances. This might be explained by the floristic and climatic conditions in South Sweden which deviate considerably from those in e.g. Germany, a feature supported by the communities' indicator figures for temperature and continentality. This refers particularly to the combination of rather low average temperatures and, except in the west, a strong thermal or hygric continentality.

The most important data on topographical and geological conditions are to be seen in Fig. 2 and 3, on climate in Tab. 1. The investigated territory belongs, from the phytogeographical point of view, to the Hercynicum (Eu-Hercynicum), to the district of "drsk vrchy". Subatlantic-montane species such as Juncus squarrosus and Festuca tenuifolia are characteristic, besides submontane forest species, peat-bog species and some relic blanket-bog species (Carex chordorrhiza, Scorpidium scorpioides, Paludella squarrosa, Meesia triquetra). The moderate xerothermic species only seldom penetrate on chalky soils up to the centrum of the territory. The vegetation is noted for many communities, however poor in species. The floating-leaved communities are developed only in fragments, although ponds cover a great area in the investigated territory (ponds used as swimming pools, unfavorable climatic conditions). No associations could be described here. The reed and tall sedge communities occupy only the sublittoral zone of the ponds. The reed swamps were classified as Scirpo-Phragmitetum W. Koch 1926, the tall sedge communities were divided into Caricetum rostratae Rbel 1912 and the Caricetum gracilis Almquist 1929 (see Tab. 3). The secondary stages of the ancient pools (rising after peat digging) and drainage channels mostly represent a mosaic of small segments. They are formed by mono-species stands or by stands extremely poor in species. The most important dominants of these stages are: Sphagnum cuspidatum, S. recurvum, Eriophorum vaginatum, Carex rostrata, C. lasiocarpa, Eriophorum angustifolium and chamaephytes. Peat-bog meadows of the alliance Caricion canescenti-fuscae Nordhagen 1936 are represented by Caricetum fuscae Br.-Bl. 1915 (Tab. 4) and Caricetum dioicae Klika et marda 1944 (Tab. 4). They are mostly of secondary origin. The semicultivated meadows formed by amelioration of peat-bog meadows were described as Carici-Festucetum rubrae ass. nova prov. (see Tab. 5). Its systematical position is not clear. The most frequent cultivated meadow of the mineral soils was identified with Trifolio-Festucetum rubrae Oberd. 1957 (alliance Arrhenatherion elatioris [Br.-Bl. 1925] W. Koch 1926). Although this association has not been hitherto mentioned from Czechoslovakia, it belongs to the widely distributed communities of the submontane zone, above all in the region of Hercynicum. The pastures are represented by two clearly cut associations (Nardo-Festucetum capillatae Klika et marda 1944 and Nardo-Juncetum squarrosi [Nordhagen 1920] Bker 1942, see Tab. 7) and as well by an insufficiently known group fo the Hygro- up to Xeronardeta. The dwarf shrub heats grow above all on the drained and deforested parts of the peat-bogs, but also on rough mineral soils (see Tab. 8). Dwarf scrub heats of mineral soils were classed with the Calluno-Antennarietum Tx. 1937, those on peat soils are noted for stages (the terminal stage of the secondary regeneration of peat-bog, degradation stage after drainage and deforestation), because there are no characteristic species here and our material is insufficient for syntaxonomic evaluation. The peat-bog communities (Sphagnetum magellanici [Malcuit 1929] Schwickerath 1933, Pino rotundatae-Sphagnetum [Kstner et Flssner 1933] Neuhusl 1969, Vaccinio uliginosi-Pinetum Kleist 1929 em. Matuszkiewicz 1962 and the montane Pinus sylvestris-Betula pubescens peat-bog forest) are only compared in the synthetical table, because they will be analysed in detail in another publication (Neuhusl Ms.). The natural spruce forests (Calamagrosti villosae-Piceetum F. K. Hartmann 1953, see Tab. 10) of the alliance Vaccinio-Piceion are bound with damp and cool terrain depressions in the investigated territory which is situated in the Fagion zone. They are spread secondarily on the dead, partly drained, margins of the peat-bogs. The cultural forests were divided, on the base of their correspondence to the natural potential vegetation, as follows: secondary spruce forests on the sites of acidophilous beech forests, (alliance Luzulo-Fagion Lohmeyer et Tx. 1954), on the sites of the beech and maple forests reech in herbs (suballiances Eu-Fagion Oberd. 1957 em. Tx. 1960 and Acerion pseudoplatani Oberd. 1957) and on the sites of acidophilous montane beech forests (Verticillato-Fagetum Oberd. 1957). No sociological analyses have been carried out in the secondary spruce forests; their classification is based on the terrain factors and the presence of rest species. Two groups of field weed communities, corresponding to the eutrophic (on chalky soils) and oligotrophic (on silicate rocks) substrates were distinguished. The differences between the Campanula rapunculoides-Myosotis arvensis community (on chalky soils) and the Apera spicaventi-Vicia tetrasperma community (on siliceous soils) can be seen in Tab. 11. Both communities show the closest dependence on the alliance Aphanion arvensis Malato-Beliz et al. 1960, however they have also a great number of species of the alliance Polygono-Chenopodion W. Koch 1926 em. Siss. 1946. Practically, no differences have been found between weed communities of the cereal and intertilled crops. The map of the real vegetation shows the distribution of the above mentioned communities in the investigated territory (see Fig. 4).

4180993| The ecology of seed germination was examined in air-conditioned boxes in the laboratory, and the sprouting conditions of seeds were investigated in an experimental plot at Prhonice. It was found that the seeds showed no marked dormancy, but that by stratification or putting of seeds into cool soil the speed and abundance of germination was enlarged, especially at low temperatures. The optimum temperatures for germinating are 10/25-30 C and 15C (see the table). At the temperature of 3 C the seeds did not germinate. The sprouting of seeds which got into the soil at the end of summer or at the beginning of autumn goes off mostly from October to November and again in spring, about the middle of April. The young plants with one pair of true leaves for the most part hibernate. In natural conditions this species reproduced only in the generative way, by seeds, in laboratory conditions the possibility of vegetative propagation by cuttings is also reported. The main way of spreading is by anemochory (steppe runners).

4179530|Changes of plant communities (or biotic communities) are classified according to their causes. The term succession is restricted in Clements' original sense to gradual directional replacemental changes of phytocenoses (or biocenoses) caused by their reaction upon the environment including soil development and a classification of succession is proposed. Gradual changes of communities caused by external factors are termed adaptive changes. The connection between succession and soil development as a unified process as well as the concept of climax as its result are discussed. A brief historical survey of the theory of succession as well as soil development is presented and definitions of some successional terms are proposed.
4179842| The lectotype of the name Malcolmia pyramidum C. Presl in Abh. Bhm. Ges. Wiss. ser. 5 (3) 439 (1845) was established in material deposited in the herbarium of the Botanical Institute of the Charles University Praha, (PRC). 
4181262|Morphological plasticity in clonal plants has received wide attention because localized plastic changes in spacer length, branching intensity and branching angle may enable clonal plants to place ramets selectively in the more favourable microhabitats within a heterogeneous environment. These responses have been interpreted in terms of foraging behaviour. Studies of morphological plasticity in clonal plants are usually carried out with one or two genotypes of a species, or with material of unknown genetic origin. Based on the concept of phenotypic plasticity, it is argued that such studies do not reveal whether plasticity in a population can be modified by natural selection. In addition, responses are often evaluated at two environmental conditions only, which may underestimate plasticity. Hence, our information on the ecological and evolutionary significance of morphological plasticity in clonal plants is still very incomplete. Two examples are given to show that stolon internode and rhizome lengths may vary considerably within an individual plant. Only a minor part of this variation may be plastic, i.e. the variation is hardly changed by the environmental conditions to which the plants are subjected. Hence, non-plastic variation in clonal morphology may exceed the degree of morphological plasticity. The non-plastic variation seems to originate from species-specific patterns of stolon and rhizome development. Marked non-plastic variation may obscure the effects of morphological plasticity on the placement pattern of ramets in the field, suggesting that plasticity in clonal morphology may not be very effective in terms of foraging for favourable patches. Possible reasons for the low levels of plasticity of clonal spacers are discussed.
4179726| Chromosome numbers are reported for two Mongolian species, Dracocephalum foetidum Bunge (2n = 12) and Koenigia islandica L. (2n = 14). The relationship of D. foetidum to D. moldavica L. 4181219|Chromosome numbers were counted in Butomus umbellatus from 99 localities in both Czech and Slovak Republics and the karyotype morphology was studied. Basic chromosome sets are asymmetrical and uniform among diploids (2n = 26) and triploids (2n = 39). Diploids occur less frequently than triploids in this region. Their clonal populations are usually fertile owing to self-compatibility. The clonal populations of triploids are self-incompatible and usually sterile. Thus, the different self-compatibility is the main biological character distinguishing diploids from triploids. Pollen of triploids is viable in spite of meiotic irregularities in pollen mother cells (PMCs). Hybridization both between cytotypes and between the different triploid genets may take place, if they occur sympatrically. Offspring having diverse chromosome numbers between diploid and triploid level can originate as the consequence of such hybridization.

4180991|Based on the study of herbarium material, a critical taxonomic account has been provided on Cardamine sect. Macrophyllum (Cruciferae) from the Asian territory of the Soviet Union. Different morphological characters were examined but special attention was paid to flowers, nectar glands, pollen grains, fruits and seeds, followed by the anatomical studies of fruits and seeds. 8 species have been recognized which are arranged in 2 subsections under Cardamine sect. Macrophyllum viz. 1. Macrophyllae (C. leucantha, C. tomentella, C. macrophylla and C. densiflora) and 2. Prorepentae (C. schinziana, C. yezoensis, C. amareaformis and C. prorepens). 4179681| Die Ergebnisse der pollenanalytischen und grossrestanalytischen Bearbeitung der See- und Torfablagerungen von Vracov (Sdmhren, Tschechoslowakei) ermglichten einen ersten Einblick in die Vegetationsentwicklung der unmittelbaren und weiteren Umgebung des ehemaligen Sees von Vracov. Besondere Aufmerksamkeit ist der sich im Pollendiagramm widerspiegelden Beeinflussung von Vegetation und Landschaft durch menschliche Ttigkeit gewidmet worden. Ferner wird die Problematik der Ursprnglichkeit und Kontinuitt der sdmhrischen xerothermen Steppenvegetation und die damit verbundene Frage nach dem Entstehen und der Entwicklung der Tschernosembden im Untersuchungsgebiet diskutiert. /// The present paper submits the first results of palaeoecological investigations carried out in the area of a former lake on the outskirts of the town of Vracov (SE Moravia - Czechoslovakia). The locality is situated by the border of the extensive subarid Pannonian Lowlands, thus having great importance for study of the vegetation history of this area. The present paper is chiefly based on pollen and macroscopic analyses of the profile DU-1-B. Although the results and conclusions offered by this paper cannot be definitive (research being still in progress) some fundamental information on several problems has already been obtained. This information concerns: (1) the development of the lake proper and the changing of its vegetation during the Late Weichselian and Flandrian; (2) the development of the neighbouring forests and of dry-land vegetation in the same period; (3) the extent and type of agriculture and of human activity in the area; (4) the steppe problem associated with the problem of the origin and evolution of the chernozem soils. 1. The origin of the former lake of Vracov is supposed to go back to the beginning of the Late-Weichselian Period. As late as the end of the Pre-boreal Period the lake was open and algengyttja was deposited on its bottom. During the Boreal and Atlantic Periods, the edges of the lake were gradually covered by Carex and Phragmites stands. In spite of some short regressions to the Carex-Phragmites stands, between the end of the Sub-boreal Period and the beginning of this century the lake was filled in by brown-moss communities. About fifty years ago the fen was drained. According to the type of sedimentation and vegetation succession, the whole period of the existence of the lake can be divided into eight phases (see p. 290, 291). 2. The pollen diagram traces the development of dry-land vegetation since the Allerd or from the end of the older Dryas. As early as in the Allerd Period an uninterrupted forest cover in the area consisting of Betula and Pinus is supposed to have existed. In the Pre-boreal Period, Quercus and Ulmus also appeared in addition to the dominants Betula and Pinus. Corylus was widespread and, in the Boreal, it reached its maximum. In the Boreal and Atlantic Periods the common type of mixed oak forests become predominant in the lowlands. Fagus and Abies and, partly, Carpinus appeared in the foothills of the Chiby Mountains. Fagus appears continuously from the Boreal, Abies from the beginning of the Pre-boreal; however, these trees attained their maximum development as late as the older Sub-atlantic Period. The final formation of the climax forests as known from today can also be dated to that time. 3. The first traces of human settlement and agriculture go back (according to the pollen diagram) to the end of the Atlantic Period. Since that time, as also shown by archeological and historical data, the region round Vracov has been continuously settled. According to the type and extent of agricultural activity revealed by pollen diagram, five stages can be distinguished: a) Neolithic and Aeneolithic Man seems to be a pastoralist using the forest for grazing his cattle, while the cereal production was limited to small patches of land round human settlements and exerted no great influence on the extent of forest cover. b) Bronze Age Man in the Sub-boreal Period began to reduce the total forest area. The extensive cereal cultivation became predominant over grazing activity. The fallows were probably used as pasture land in this period. c) In the Iron Age, Roman Period and during the Great Migration Period (the Older Subatlantic) the area of cultivated soil was substantially enlarged. The most accessible and most productive soils were apparently deforested in that period. The extensive cultivation of cereals still predominated, but new cultivated plants seem to be introduced in that time (Cannabis, Vitis vinifera, Juglans). d) In the Middle Ages (the older part of the Younger Subatlantic Period) the human settlements spread and even less accessible and less productive soils were deforested in the area of the Chiby foothills, originally covered by Quercus-Carpinus and Fagus-Abies forests. The still extensive cultivation of cereals, together with fallows used for grazing spread to new large regions. e) The decline of agriculture towards the end of the Middle Ages was succeeded by a stage of great agricultural expansion, in which the land was much more intensely cultivated than before. Consequently, the remaining forest stands were used as pasture lands. The pollen diagram reveals the introduction of Fagopyrum and systematic cultivation of Cannabis. 4. The uninterrupted forest cover of the area lasted from the Allerd to the very end of the Atlantic Period. This is the reason why the existence of open steppe vegetation producing chernozem soils on loess during the Boreal or Atlantic Periods (as suggested by existing hypotheses) can be ruled out. A detailed discussion is devoted to the history of steppe vegetation during the Flandrian and to the problem of the origin and evolution of the chernozem soils. New discoveries seem to suggest that the chernozem soils could originate or remain in existence also under certain forest vegetation in suitable climatic and vegetational conditions of Central Europe. 
4181443| The presence of various flavonoids, naphthodianthrones and phloroglucinol derivatives was studied in the natural pentaploid hybrid H. maculatum Crantz subsp. maculatum  H. perforatum L. The hybrid taxon was shown to have secondary metabolites in common with both putative parents thus confirming its parentage. Morphological and nomenclatural questions are briefly discussed. 
4180657|On the north shore of Lake Balaton four study areas were selected with different levels of mineral nutrient supply (two of them are at sewage inflows, one is at the mouth of a natural watercourse, and one is unaffected by water inflow). Studies were made on the development of Phragmites australis (Cav.) Trin. ex Steudel stands. Monthly levels of N, P, K, Na, Ca and Mg in the organs (leaf-blade, leaf-sheath, culm, aquatic root, rhizome and root) of reed were determined from April to October in 1980. Differences were detected between the four study areas in the shoot height, mass, growth rate and element contents. In the aboveground organs, the levels of N, P, and K showed a decrease all through the growing season, but Ca and Mg rose to a peak before declining for the rest of the season. In the underground organs the levels of N and P decreased to a minimum in June to July and thereafter the quantities of these elements gradually increased. In the most heavily contaminated area (area IV), significantly higher levels of tissue N, P and K were found.

In dieser Mitteilung werden die Studienergebnisse ber die Verbreitungsbiologie und Keimung der Virga-Frchte angefrt. Sie berichtet auch ber das Vorkommen und die Verbreitung dieser Art bei der Stadt Jlov bei Praha in den letzten 6 Jahren und gibt die Unterschiede zwischen der fremden Art Virga strigosa und der einheimischen Art Virga pilosa an (Synonymik siehe bei Holub 1964). 
4179631| Junco inflexi-Menthetum longifoliae stellt auf dem Gebiet der Tschechoslowakei eine sowohl floristisch als auch kologisch zeimlich gut ausgeprgte Assoziation dar. Es trgt den Kennzeichnenden Charakter der Kontaktgesellschaften mit Bindung an nasse bis wechselfeuchtige Bden, deren Sorptionskomplex mit Ionen zweiwertiger Basen gesttigt ist. Es sind zwei Subassoziationen angefhrt: Junco inflexi-Menthetum longifoliae typicum und Junco inflexi-Menthetum longifoliae caricetosum. An analogen Standorten mit saureren Bden und nicht vllig gesttigtem Sorptionskomplex entwickelt sich die Assoziation Epilobio-Juncetum (effusi). /// Junco inflexi-Menthetum longifoliae which has been investigated in various parts of Czechoslovakia represents a rather uniform community with comparatively true characteristic species - Juncus inflexus, Mentha longifolia, and in the investigated areas also Hypericum tetrapterum. The specific composition in general is also characteristic - first of all there is the constant share of species bound more strictly to the alliance Agropyro-Rumicion crispi as well as of species equipped with a wider cenotic amplitude, the optimum of which is situated within the units of the class Plantaginetea maioris. The species group from other cenological units is numerous, indeed, but these species are mostly not very constant. Within the association there are two subassociations to be distinguished: Junco inflexi-Menthetum longifoliae typicum (without any differential species) which is bound to lower sites, and Junco inflexi-Menthetum longifoliae caricetosum stellulatae with a number of differential species; it is differentiated from the ecological standpoint, too. The last-mentioned subassociation simultaneously represents an ecological mountain race. Junco inflexi-Menthetum longifoliae is a community on the contact of relatively moist and dry habitats; usually it surrounds spring areas on slopes, or depressions of riverain sites which are flooded for short periods only. Beside the moist or temporarily waterlogged soil (soil types gley or anmoor), another important condition for the rise of the association is high base-saturation of the soil sorption complex; this circumstance evidently contributes to higher nitrate production in the soil. Epilobio-Juncetum (effusi) arises on habitats of analogous character, but with more acid soil, in which the sorption complex is not so saturated with bases and the Al
4179738|The division of Cuscuta s.l. into 4 genera, based mainly on floral morphology, is corroborated by their embryology. Several new combinations in Monogynella and Grammica are proposed.
4180987|Attempts have been made to reveal the survival strategies of the two forms of Trianthema portulacastrum. These morphs, viz rubra and flava, do not show any remarkable difference in their morphology, phenology and water relations. Metabolically, rubra form is more hardy than flava form, because of lesser water loss, higher water retention capacity, high protein content and higher levels of proline accumulation at different stages of plant growth. Seed germination studies revealed the presence of hard seed coatedness in both merphs, being more in the flava form.
4180558| A description of some woodless plant communities occurring in the central part of the Isla de la Juventud is presented. Most of the communities originated from Pinus forests. The substrate is formed by oligotrophic white sand. According to the plant composition and the corresponding water regime, three classes were established in the area under study: the Hydrolaeetea nigricaulis Baltov-Tulkov 1985; the Parvirhynschosporo-Eriocauletea Borhidi in Baltov-Tulkov et Capote 1985 and the Curatello-Byrsonimetea Borhidi ex Baltov-Tulkov et Surli 1983. The communities of the first class, poor in species, are bound to periodically inundated depressions. The second class, the Parvirhynchosporo-Eriocauletea, includes communities occurring in area with inundations shallower than those in the first class. The third class, the Curatello-Byrsonimetea, includes savanna communities of periodically dry sites.

4181393|Variance deficit in the number of species per sampling unit, as compared to a null model with species occurring independently of each other has been considered by various authors to be evidence for niche limitation. I show that simpler mechanisms could explain this phenomenon. Of those, the competition of individuals for space limits the number of individuals per sampling unit, resulting in decrease of variance in species richness. Testing the proportions of species belonging to various guilds seems to be more ecologically interesting, although here also the variance deficit can hardly be taken as reliable evidence for niche limitation.
4181164|The paper summarizes data concerning the biology and ecology of Oenanthe aquatica. The species is commonly distributed all over Czechoslovakia, from lowlands to the submontane belt, especially in fishpond and river basins. O. aquatica shows no special relationship to the chemical and physical soil properties, and is well adapted to habitats with a changing water level. The reproduction of O. aquatica depends on emerging of the bottom. The most developed populations are formed by biennial plants and arise in the year following summer or autumn drainage.

4180688|Seed survival of Avena fatua L. var. fatua at various depths (0 to 50 cm) in a degraded chernozem was studied over a period of eight years. Statistical evaluation showed that seeds survived significantly during the first two years at depths of 0 to 20 cm, while at depths of 30 to 50 cm seeds statistically survived in the course of four years. After six years significant withering was observed within the whole soil profile, though 1% of seeds remained viable even until the eighth year. A tendency for prolonged survival of small seeds, and partly of medium ones, was observed in deeper soil layers in the sixth and seventh year.

4180411| This part of the study, referring to the previous syntaxonomic part (Kov 1981), presents the results of a synecological examination of nine grassland communities of the Labe river basin covering roughly the following gradient of the alluvial hydrosere: the Cerastio arvensi-Festucetum trachyphyllae trifolietosum pratensis, the Arrhenatheretum elatioris typicum, the Alopecuretum pratensis, the Stellario-Deschampsietum caespitosae phalaridetosum, the Serratulo-Festucetum commutatae, the Molinietum coeruleae brometosum, the Angelico-Cirsietum oleracei, the Caricetum gracilis typicum, the Caricetum buekii. The long-term study of ground-water level fluctuations showed their close connection to other characteristics of the meadow soils (soil type, moisture content, granulometric composition, capillary water-holding capacity, porosity, acidity, mineral nutrient contents, microbial activity, soil temperature) as well as to the development and distribution of the grassland communities associated with ecosystems of river alluvia. The formation and dynamics of the vegetation in the large river floodplain (at present exposed to the impact of far-reaching hydrological alteration) are explained as a consequence of changes in the natural ecocycles supporting the long-term stable character of the large river basin within the landscape.
